Intuitive Knowledge (Hadsiyyat) and Its Assimilation to Experiential Knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya assimilates intuitive to experiential knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's assimilation of intuitive knowledge (hadsiyyat) to experiential knowledge (mujarrabat) and identify the distinctive feature of non-deliberate repetition.

Core Idea
Intuitive knowledge is just experiential knowledge without deliberate human repetition.

Ibn Taymiyya concludes his discussion by dealing with intuitive knowledge (hadsiyyat), which logicians classify separately. He argues that it is essentially the same as experiential knowledge, except that the repetition leading to the universal judgment is not under human control but occurs naturally. This lesson consolidates your understanding of how wide the category of experiential knowledge is.

Guided Path
1
Find Ibn Taymiyya's description of intuitive knowledge
He identifies it as knowledge from non-deliberate repetition, e.g., astronomical intuitions.
2
Identify the examples
Moon's light from the sun, fixed stars' single sphere, planets' different spheres.
3
Compare with experiential knowledge
Both involve sense of particulars and intellectual inference; difference lies in the cause of repetition (human action vs. natural occurrence).
4
Check the logicians' classification
Some call these also 'mujarrabat'; Ibn Taymiyya agrees and notes the terminological overlap.
5
Assess the implication
If hadsiyyat are included, then the category of empirical knowledge is broader than the logicians allow, and they are valid for burhan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هؤلاء ما لم يتواتر عند غيرهم ولم يجربوه. ولكن قد يتفقان في الجنس، كما يجرب قوم بعض الأدوية ويجرب الآخرون جنس تلك الأدوية فيتفق في معرفة الجنس، لا معرفة عين المجرّب. ثم هم مع هذا، يقولون في المنطق: إن المتواترات، والمجربات، لا يقوم بها والحدسيات تختص بمن عَلِمها، فلا يقوم منها برهان على غيره. فيقال لهم: وكذلك برهان على المشمومات والمَذُوقات والملموسات. بل اشتراك الناس في المتواترات أكثر. فإن الخبر المتواتر ينقله عدد كثير فيكثر السامعون له ويشتركون في سماعه العدد من الكثير، لا سيما إذا كان العدد الكثير مئين وألوفاً فبطائفة من هؤلاء يحصل العلم المتواتر. فإذا نَقَل هؤلاء القوم، وهؤلاء القوم، وهؤلاء لقوم، حصل العلم المتواتر لأمم لا يُحصي عددهم إلا الله بخلاف ما يدرك بالحواس فإنه يختص بمن أحسه. فإذا قال «رأيتُ» أو «سمعتُ» أو «ذقتُ» أو «لمستُ» أو «شممتُ» فكيف يمكنه أن يقيم من برهاناً على غيره؟ ولو قدر أنه شاركه في تلك الحسيات عدد فلا يلزم من ذلك أن يكون غيرُهم أحَسَّها. ولا يمكن علمها لمن لم يُحِسَّها إلا بطريق الخبر. فإذا ادعوا أن «الخبر المتواتر مختص بالحسيات، فلا يقوم به البرهان على المنازع» فالحسيات أعظم اختصاصاً، فيلزم أن لا يقوم بها برهان على المنازع وليس في الحسيات أكثر اشتراكاً من «الرؤية»، فإن الناس يشتركون في رؤية الأنوار العلوية، كالشمس والقمر والكواكب، ولكن مواد البرهان لا يختص بذلك. وإن قالوا الحسيات تحصل بالاشتراك في جنسها، كاشتراك الناس في قد تحصل معرفة الألوان والطعوم والروائح والحرارة والبرودة، وإن لم يكن عين ما أحسه بالاشتراك هؤلاء هو عين ما أحسه هؤلاء، لكن اشتركا في الجنس قيل: والمتواترات والمجربات قد يشتركون في جنسها كما تقدم. بل وجود الشبع والرّي عقيب الأكل والشرب هو من المجربات، والناس يشتركون في جنسه. وكذلك وجود اللذة بذلك، وبالجماع وغير ذلك، بما إذا فعله الإنسان وجد عقيبه أثراً من الآثار، ثم يتكرر ذلك حتى يَعْلَم أن ذاك سبب هذا الأثر، فهذا هو التجربيات. المقام الرابع - الوجه الثامن: كون الحسيات لا يقوم بها برهان على المنازع والقضايا الظنية أصلها التجربيات، وهو من هذا الباب. فإن المراد أنه إذا استعمل الدواء الفلاني وجد زوال المرض أو حصل به ألم المرض. فوجود المرض بهذا و وجود زواله بهذا هو من التجربيات وكذلك الآلام واللذات التي تحصل بالمشمومات والمسموعات والمرئيات والملموسات فإن الحس ينال كذا ويسمع هذا، ويذوق هذا، ويلمس هذا ثم وجود اللذة في النفس هو من الوجديات المعلومة بالحس الباطن، وهو من جنس الحسيات الظاهرة. وأما الاعتقاد الكلي القائم في النفس من أن هذا الجنس يحصل به اللذة، وهذا التجربيات مركبة من الجنس يحصل به الألم فهذا من التجربيات، إذ الحسيات الظاهرة والباطنة ليس فيها الحس والعقل شيء كلي. فالقضاء الكلي الذي يقوم بالقلب هو مركب من الحس والعقل، وهو التجربيات، كما في اعتقاد حصول الشبع والري بما يعرف من المأكولات والمشروبات والموتِ والمرض بما يعرف من السموم القتالة والأسباب الممرضة، وزوال ذلك بالأسباب المعروفة وكل هذا من القضايا التجربية. فالحس به تعرف الأمور المعينة، ثم إذا تكررت مرة بعد مرة أدرك العقل أن هذا بسبب القدر المشترك الكلي، فقضى قضاء كلياً أن هذا يورث اللذة الفُلانية، وهذا يورث الألم الفلاني. والحَدْسِيّات هي كذلك. فبالحس يعرف أعيانها، ثم يتكرر فيعلم بالعقل القدرُ المشترك. لكن ذلك التكرر لا يكون بفعل الإنسان، بل هو كما يعرف من الأمور الحدسيات السماوية، مثل أن يرى اختلاف أنوار القمر عند اختلاف مقابلته للشمس، فَيَحْدِسُ أن ضوءه مستفاد منها. ومثل ما يرى الثوابت لا تختلف حركتها بالطول والعرض، بل حركتها حركة واحدة فيُحْدِس أن فلكها واحد، وإلا فيجوز أن يكون لكل واحد فلكاً حركته مثل حركة الآخر. ومثل ما يرى اختلاف حركات السبعة، فيحدس عن اختلاف أفلاكها. وهذا يسمى في اللغة تجربيات. وكثير منهم أيضاً يسميه «تجربيات»، ولا يجعل قسماً غير «المجربات». وبالجملة الأمورُ العادية، سواء كان سبب العادة إرادةً نفسانية أو قوة طبيعية، كون العاديات من باب التجربيات فالعلم بكونها كلية هو من التجربيات، أو الحدسيات - إن جعلت نوعاً آخر.
These are those that have not been recurrently transmitted to others nor have they been experienced. But they may agree in genus, just as some people experiment with certain medicines and others experiment with the genus of those medicines, so they agree in knowledge of the genus, not knowledge of the specific thing experimented upon. Then despite this, they say in logic: 'Indeed, recurrent reports and experiential data do not provide a proof, and intuitive matters are specific to those who know them, so a proof cannot be established from them for others.' So it is said to them: Likewise, a proof cannot be established upon smelled, tasted, and touched things. Rather, people's sharing in recurrent reports is greater. For the recurrently transmitted report is transmitted by a large number, so the listeners to it become many and they share in hearing it from many people, especially if the large number is in hundreds and thousands, so by a group of these people recurrent knowledge is obtained. So if this group transmits, and this group, and this group, recurrent knowledge is obtained for nations whose number no one knows except God, unlike what is perceived by the senses, for it is specific to the one who sensed it. So if he says 'I saw' or 'I heard' or 'I tasted' or 'I touched' or 'I smelled', how can he establish a proof for others? And if one supposes that a number shared in those sensory perceptions, it does not follow that others have sensed them. Nor can they be known by those who have not sensed them except by way of report. So if they claim that 'recurrent report is specific to sensory matters, so a proof cannot be established by it for the opponent,' then sensory matters are even more specific, so it follows that a proof cannot be established by them for the opponent. And there is nothing in sensory matters more shared than 'sight', for people share in seeing celestial lights like the sun, moon, and stars, but the materials of proof are not specific to that. And if they say that sensory matters are obtained by sharing in their genus, like people's sharing in the fact that knowledge of colors, tastes, smells, heat and cold may be obtained, even if the specific thing sensed by these is not the specific thing sensed by those, but they share in the genus, it is said: Recurrent reports and experiential data may be shared in their genus as previously mentioned. Rather, the occurrence of satiety and thirst after eating and drinking is from experiential data, and people share in its genus. Likewise the occurrence of pleasure from that, and from intercourse and other things, such that when a person does it he finds an effect after it, then it is repeated until he knows that that is the cause of this effect, this is experiential data. The fourth station - the eighth aspect: That sensory matters do not provide a proof for the opponent. And speculative propositions have their origin in experiential data, and it is from this chapter. For the meaning is that when he uses such-and-such a medicine, he finds the removal of illness or the occurrence of pain from illness. So the occurrence of illness by this and the occurrence of its removal by this is from experiential data. Likewise the pains and pleasures that occur through smells, sounds, sights, and touches, for the sense obtains such, hears this, tastes this, touches this, then the occurrence of pleasure in the soul is from subjective experiences known by inner sense, and it is of the genus of external sensory matters. As for the universal belief established in the soul that this genus brings pleasure, and this brings pain, this is from experiential data, for external and internal sensory matters do not contain anything universal by sense and intellect. So the universal judgment that arises in the heart is composed of sense and intellect, and it is experiential data, as in the belief of obtaining satiety and thirst from what is known of foods and drinks, and death and illness from what is known of deadly poisons and harmful causes, and their removal by known causes, and all of this is from experiential propositions. For by sense, particular things are known, then when they are repeated time after time, the intellect perceives that this is due to the universal common factor, so it makes a universal judgment that this brings such-and-such pleasure, and this brings such-and-such pain. And intuitive matters are likewise. For by sense their particulars are known, then they are repeated and the intellect knows the common factor. But that repetition does not occur by human action; rather it is like what is known of celestial intuitive matters, such as seeing the difference in the moon's light according to its differing opposition to the sun, so one intuits that its light is derived from it. And like seeing that the fixed stars do not differ in their motion in longitude and latitude, but rather their motion is one motion, so one intuits that their sphere is one, otherwise it would be possible for each to have a sphere with a motion like the other's motion. And like seeing the difference in the motions of the seven planets, so one intuits the difference of their spheres. And this is called in language 'experiential data'. And many of them also call it 'experiential data', and do not make it a division other than 'experiential data'. In summary, customary matters, whether the cause of the custom is a psychic will or a natural power, that customary matters are from the category of experiential data, so the knowledge that they are universal is from experiential data, or from intuitive data - if made another type.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's *Radd Mantiqiyyin* engages in a critical refutation of the logicians' epistemological claims. The target is the assertion found in Aristotelian logic that certain types of propositions—specifically, recurrent reports (*mutawatirat*), experiential data (*mujarribat*), and intuitive judgments (*hadsiyat*)—cannot serve as premises for a demonstration (*burhan*) that commands universal assent, because they are either too particular or depend on the individual experiencer. Ibn Taymiyya begins by noting that the logicians themselves admit that these types of knowledge are valid for those who possess them, but they claim that a *burhan* cannot be built from them for others. He then draws a parallel: if that is the case, then it applies even more strongly to sensory knowledge (*hissiyat*), which is even more particular. Yet the logicians themselves use sensory knowledge (e.g., in natural science) without objection. He argues that recurrent reports are actually more widely shared than sensory perceptions, because a large number of people transmit and receive them, making them publicly known, while sensory perceptions are private. Thus the logicians' position is inconsistent: they reject recurrent reports as proof but implicitly accept sensory experience, which is even less shareable. Ibn Taymiyya then addresses a possible counter: that sensory knowledge can be shared in genus (e.g., everyone knows colors, even if not the same specific color). He responds that the same is true of recurrent reports and experiential data—people share in the genus of such knowledge, as when they know that eating causes satiety or that certain medicines cure disease. He then elaborates on how experiential knowledge arises: through repeated observation of particular events, the intellect perceives a universal causal connection. This composite of sense and intellect yields universal judgments, which are the basis of empirical propositions (*qadaya tajribiyya*). Intuitive knowledge (*hadsiyat*) follows a similar pattern, but without deliberate human repetition; examples include astronomical insights like deducing that moonlight comes from the sun. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that customary regularities, whether psychological or natural, are ultimately grounded in experiential data, so they can serve as premises for reasoning. Throughout, he undercuts the logicians' attempt to restrict the materials of demonstration, defending a broader empiricist epistemology rooted in common human experience.

Key Terms
الحدسيات
التجربيات
القدر المشترك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what distinguishes hadsiyyat from mujarrabat?
A) Hadsiyyat are based on sense perception, mujarrabat are not.
B) Hadsiyyat involve repetition not caused by human action; mujarrabat involve deliberate repetition.
C) Hadsiyyat are less certain than mujarrabat.
D) Hadsiyyat are a type of mutawatirat.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya collapses the distinction between intuitive and experiential knowledge, arguing both arise from the same epistemic process, thus broadening the valid premises for demonstration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Give an example from Islamic astronomy or medicine that would be classified as hadsiyya according to Ibn Taymiyya, and explain why it shares the same epistemic structure as mujarrabat.
?
Using Ibn Taymiyya's framework, show that the knowledge that 'the sun rises every day' is a form of experiential or intuitive knowledge and can serve as a premise for a theological argument.

Refuting Suhrawardi's Use of Quran to Deny Change
Author refutes al-Suhrawardi's use of a Quranic verse to argue for the world's immutability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate Ibn Taymiyya's critique of al-Suhrawardi's argument from the Quran against change, distinguishing between 'ādah (habit) and sunnah (divine way).

Core Idea
God's unchangeable sunnah is about justice, not natural regularity.

Al-Suhrawardi, a philosopher known for his heretical views, attempted to use a Quranic verse to argue that the world never changes, citing the sun's consistent rising and setting as God's habit. In this passage, the author refutes this by clarifying that God's unchangeable sunnah pertains specifically to His rewarding believers and punishing disbelievers, not to all natural phenomena. He invokes the principle of divine wisdom (ḥikmah) to show that this sunnah is rooted in justice, and that miracles (khariq al-'ādah) are empirically known and do not contradict it. This lesson will guide you through the logical structure of this refutation and its implications for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify Suhrawardi's Claim
Locate Suhrawardi's argument in the passage: he uses a Quranic verse to assert that the world does not change, using the sun's daily rising and setting as an example of God's habit.
Suhrawardi's claim is an atheistic attempt to deny miracles and change.
2
Isolate the Quranic Verse and Its Context
Find the verse from Surah Fatir (35:43) quoted by the author. Note the author's interpretation: the verse refers specifically to God's sunnah concerning the fate of nations, not to all natural regularities.
The verse in question: 'So you will not find for the way of Allah any substitution, and you will not find for the way of Allah any change.'
3
Distinguish 'Adah from Sunnah
The author distinguishes between 'ādah (habit) and sunnah (divine way). 'Adah refers to natural regularities that can be broken (miracles), while sunnah refers to God's consistent practice in rewarding and punishing, which is unchangeable because it stems from His wisdom.
This distinction is crucial: Suhrawardi conflates the two.
4
Understand the Role of Divine Wisdom (Ḥikmah)
The author argues that God's will is wise, not arbitrary. A wise agent's will necessitates equality between similar things. Therefore, God's sunnah of rewarding believers and punishing disbelievers is consistent, but changes that wisdom requires are also part of His sunnah.
This refutes the Ash'ari view of arbitrary will that prefers one similar over another without reason.
5
Evaluate the Refutation's Coherence
Check if the author's distinction holds: does it successfully defend the possibility of miracles while maintaining God's consistency? Consider how the principle of equality between similars (mutamāthilāt) works in this context.
The critique is internally valid: it uses the same Quranic verse to support a different, more nuanced position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أراد بعض الملاحدة كالسُّهروردي المقتول في كتابه المبدأ والمعاد الذي سماه «الألواح العمادية» أن يجعل له دليلاً من القرآن والسنة على إلحاده. فاستدل على عدم تغير العالم بهذه الآية على أن العالم لا يتغير، بل لا تزال الشمس تطلع وتغرب لأنها عادة الله . فيقال له : انخراق العادات أمر معلوم بالحس والمشاهدة بالجملة. وقد أخبر في غير موضع أن سبحانه لم يخلق العالم عبئاً وباطلاً، بل لأجل الجزاء. فكان هذا من سنته الجميلة، وهو جزاؤه الناسَ بأعمالهم في الدار الآخرة، كما أخبر به من نصر أوليائه وعقوبة أعدائه . فبَعْتُ الناس للجزاء هو من هذه السنة. وهو لم يخبر بأن كل عادة لا تنتقض ، بل أخبر عن السنة التي هي عواقب أفعال العباد بإثابة أولياءه ونصرهم على الأعداء . فهذه هي التي أخبر أنه لن يوجد لها تبديل ولا تحويل، كما قال: ﴿ فَهَلْ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَّا سُنَتَ الْأَوَّلِينَ فَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللهِ تَبْدِيلًا وَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللهِ تَحْوِيلًا ﴾ [سورة فاطر : ٤٣] . وذلك لأن العادة تتبع إرادة الفاعل، وإرادة الفاعل الحكيم هي إرادة حكيمة، إرادة الحكيم تقتضي التسوية فتسوي بين المتماثلات ولن يوجد لهذه السنة تبديل ولا تحويل، وهو إكرام أهل ولايته وطاعته ونصر رسله والذين آمنوا على المكذبين فهذه السنة تقتضيها حكمته سبحانه فلا انتقاض لها، بخلاف ما اقتضت حكمته تغييره. فذاك، تغييره من أيضاً ومن سنته التي لا يوجد لها تبديل ولا تحويل. لكن في هذه الآيات ردُّ على مَنْ يجعله يفعل بمجرد إرادة تُرجّح أحد المتماثلين بلا مُرجّح. فإن هؤلاء ليس عندهم له سنة لا تتبدل، ولا حكمة تقصد وهذا خلاف النصوص والعقول . فإن السنة تقتضي تماثل الآحاد وأن حكم الشيء حكم نظيره ، فيقتضي التسوية بين المتماثلات . وهذا خلاف قولهم .
And some atheists like al-Suhrawardi, the executed one, intended in his book 'al-Mabda' wa al-Ma'ad' which he called 'al-Alwah al-Imadiyya' to make for himself a proof from the Quran and Sunnah for his heresy. So he argued using this verse for the non-change of the world: that the world does not change, rather the sun always rises and sets because it is a habit of God. So it is said to him: The breaking of habits is known by sense and observation in general. And He informed in more than one place that He, exalted, did not create the world in vain and falsehood, but for the sake of recompense. So this was from His beautiful way, and it is His recompensing people for their deeds in the hereafter, as He informed of His support of His allies and punishment of His enemies. So sending people for recompense is from this way. And He did not inform that every habit is not broken, but He informed about the way which is the consequences of the actions of servants by rewarding His allies and supporting them against enemies. This is what He informed that there will not be for it any substitution or change, as He said: {Do they await except the way of the former ones? Then you will not find for the way of Allah any substitution, and you will not find for the way of Allah any change} [Surah Fatir: 43]. And that is because habit follows the will of the agent, and the will of the wise agent is a wise will. The will of the wise necessitates equality, so He equalizes between similar things, and there will not be for this way any substitution or change. And it is honoring the people of His loyalty and obedience and supporting His messengers and those who believe against the deniers. So this way is necessitated by His wisdom, exalted, so it is not broken, contrary to what His wisdom necessitated to change. So that, its change is also from His way which does not have substitution or change. But in these verses is a refutation of those who make Him act by mere will that prefers one of two similars without a preponderant. For these, they do not have for Him a way that does not change, nor a wisdom that is intended. And this contradicts the texts and intellects. For the way necessitates the similarity of individuals and that the ruling of a thing is the ruling of its like, so it necessitates equality between similars. And this contradicts their statement.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of al-Suhrawardi's atheistic argument. The author first states that al-Suhrawardi used a Quranic verse to claim that the world never changes, arguing that the sun always rises and sets as God's habit. The author responds by explaining that miracles (khariq al-'adat) are known by sensory experience, and that God's unchangeable way (sunnah) pertains specifically to His rewarding believers and punishing disbelievers, not to all natural phenomena. He cites the verse from Surah Fatir to support that this specific sunnah has no substitution or change. The author then delves into the philosophy of divine will: a wise agent's will necessitates equality between similar things, so God's sunnah in rewarding the righteous is consistent. However, changes that God's wisdom decrees are also part of His unchangeable way. The passage concludes by refuting those who claim God acts by arbitrary will without reason, arguing that this contradicts the sunnah which requires justice between similars. Throughout, the author uses Quranic examples and logical reasoning to defend the Islamic concept of divine wisdom and the possibility of miracles.

Key Terms

عادة
إرادة
حكمة
متماثلات

D) The sun rises and sets without change

Key Takeaway
God's unchangeable sunnah pertains to His justice in rewarding and punishing, not to all natural regularities, allowing for miracles while preserving divine consistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the distinction between 'ādah and sunnah from this lesson, analyze the following claim: 'If God's sunnah never changes, then the Prophet Muhammad's night journey (Isra') could not have happened.' Determine whether this objection is valid based on the author's framework.
?
Identify a Quranic verse that mentions God's sunnah (e.g., Surah Al-Imran: 137). Explain how this verse should be interpreted according to the author's criteria, distinguishing between natural habits and divine justice.

Tawatur of the Prophets vs. Tawatur of the Philosophers
Author establishes that prophetic tawatur surpasses philosophical tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the epistemological strength of prophetic tawatur with philosophical tawatur using Ibn Taymiyya's historical argument.

Core Idea
Prophetic tawatur is historically more foundational than philosophical reports.

Ibn Taymiyya confronts philosophers who claim that mass-transmitted reports (mutawātirāt) cannot be demonstrated against opponents. He argues that the tawatur of the prophets, especially Muhammad, is so well-known that it serves as a chronological anchor for world history. This lesson unpacks his evidence for why prophetic tawatur surpasses philosophical tawatur in certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim
Find the part where the author describes what philosophers say about mutawātirāt: they claim that mass-transmitted reports cannot be established by demonstration against an opponent, aiming to dismiss prophetic miracles.
This is a rhetorical tactic to undermine the authority of prophetic traditions.
2
Examine Ibn Taymiyya's counter-claim
He asserts by necessity (ḍarūra) that the tawatur of Muhammad's emergence and the Quran is greater than that of all philosophers combined. Note the use of 'by necessity' to indicate self-evident knowledge.
3
Analyze his evidence from historical dating
Ibn Taymiyya points out that prophetic events are used as chronological references (e.g., Hijri calendar, dating before Christ), showing universal recognition. Philosophers like Aristotle are only known through their association with figures like Alexander, highlighting the secondary nature of philosophical tawatur.
This is an inductive argument: widespread use as a dating system implies widespread knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمقصود هنا الكلام على الفلاسفة. فنقول : معلوم أن من شياطينهم من يقول : المتواترات لا يقوم بها البرهان على المنازع ليُدْخِل في ذلك ما تواتر عن الأنبياء - صلوات الله عليهم - من الآيات والبراهين، والمعجزات، التي بعثوا بها، كما يُدخلون ما أُخِذ عن الأنبياء من المقبولات . فيقال لهم : من المعلوم بالاضطرار أن تواثر خروج محمد ـ صلى الله عليه وسلم - ومجيئه بهذا القرآن أعظم عند أهل الأرض من تواتر وجود الفلاسفة كلهم، فضلاً عما يُخبرون به من القضايا التجربية والحدسية التي استدلوا بها على الطبيعيات والفلكيات . وكذلك ما تواتر من سائر معجزاته وما تواتر من أخبار موسى والمسيح - صلوات الله عليهما. هذا معلوم عند الناس أعظم من تواتر وجود أولئك فضلاً عن تَوَاتُر ما يخبرون به . ولهذا صار ظهور الأنبياء مما تؤرّخ به الحوادث في العالم لظهور أمرهم عند الخاصة والعامة. فإن التأريخ يكون بالحادث المشهور الذي يشترك الناس فيه ليعرفوا به كم مضى بعده ،وقبله كما أن النهار يعرف بطلوع الشمس والشهر بالهلال، لأنه نور ظاهر يشترك الناس في رؤيته . ولهذا جعل عمرُ تأريخ المسلمين من الهجرة النبوية، فإنها أظهرُ أحوال الرسول المشهورة، وهو خروجه من بلد إلى بلد، وبها أعزّ الله الإسلام. وكانت العرب قبل الإسلام تؤرّخ بالحوادث المشهورة، وكذلك الروم، والفرس والقِبْط، وسائر الأمم، يؤرخون مثل ذلك فنحن اليوم إذا أردنا أن نعرف زمان واحد من هؤلاء المتفلسفة قلنا كان قبل المسيح بكذا وكذا سنة . بل أرسطو إنما عُرف زمانه لأنه قد عرف أنه كان وزير الإسكندر بن فيلبس المقدوني، ملك اليونان. وكانوا مشركين يعبدون الكواكب والأصنام، ويُعانون السحر - أرسطو وملكه وغيرهما. وهذا الإسكندر لما جاء إلى الشام أيام بني إسرائيل غَلَب عليهم. فذكروا أنه طلب أن يُكتب في التوراة فقالوا: «ما يمكن هذا»، فقال: اجعلوا لي تأريخاً»، فصار التأريخ الرومي الذي تؤرّخ به اليهود والنصارى مؤرخاً به .
And the intention here is to speak about the philosophers. So we say: It is known that among their devils are those who say: The mass-transmitted reports cannot be established by demonstration against the opponent, in order to include in that what has been transmitted from the prophets - peace be upon them - of signs, proofs, and miracles with which they were sent, just as they include what has been taken from the prophets of accepted sayings. So it is said to them: It is known by necessity that the mass transmission of the emergence of Muhammad - may Allah bless him and grant him peace - and his coming with this Quran is greater among the people of the earth than the mass transmission of the existence of all the philosophers, let alone the empirical and intuitive propositions they use to argue for natural and celestial phenomena. Likewise, what has been mass-transmitted of his other miracles and what has been mass-transmitted of the reports of Moses and Jesus - peace be upon them. This is known among people as greater than the mass transmission of the existence of those, let alone the mass transmission of what they report. For this reason, the appearance of the prophets became something by which events are dated in the world, due to the prominence of their matter among the elite and common people. For dating is by the famous event which people share in order to know how much time has passed after it and before it, just as the day is known by the rising of the sun and the month by the crescent, because it is an apparent light that people share in seeing. And for this reason, Umar established the dating of Muslims from the Prophetic Hijra, for it is the most prominent of the well-known states of the Messenger, which is his departure from one land to another, and by it Allah honored Islam. The Arabs before Islam used to date by famous events, and likewise the Romans, the Persians, the Copts, and all nations date by such things. So today, if we want to know the time of one of these philosophers, we say he was before Christ by so many years. Rather, Aristotle's time is only known because it was known that he was the vizier of Alexander son of Philip the Macedonian, king of the Greeks. They were polytheists worshipping planets and idols, and practicing magic - Aristotle, his king, and others. And when this Alexander came to Syria in the days of the Children of Israel, he overcame them. They mentioned that he asked to be written in the Torah, and they said, 'This is not possible.' So he said, 'Make a dating for me,' and so the Roman dating came to be, by which Jews and Christians date.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument against philosophers who claim that mass-transmitted reports (tawatur) cannot be demonstrated against opponents, in order to dismiss prophetic miracles. The author counters by stating that the tawatur of Muhammad's emergence and the Quran is far greater and more certain than that of all philosophers combined. He supports this by noting that prophetic events are used as chronological reference points for world history, such as the Hijri calendar established by Umar. The author explains that dating originates from universally known events, like the rising of the sun or the crescent moon. The Hijra was chosen because it was the most prominent event in the Prophet's life. In contrast, the dating of philosophers like Aristotle relies on their connection to historical figures like Alexander the Great, who was a polytheist and magician. The author further notes that Alexander sought to be recorded in the Torah, and when refused, initiated the Roman calendar used by Jews and Christians. Thus, the tawatur of prophetic traditions is epistemologically superior.

Key Terms
متواترات
تواتر
برهان
اضطرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what evidence supports the superior tawatur of prophetic traditions over philosophical traditions?
A) Prophetic traditions are supported by syllogistic demonstrations
B) Prophetic events are used as historical dating systems
C) Philosophers admitted the weakness of their own traditions
D) The Quran explicitly states the superiority of prophetic knowledge

Key Takeaway
The tawatur of prophetic events is epistemologically superior to philosophical tawatur because it is historically foundational and known by necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the fact that the Hijri calendar is based on the Prophet's migration (hijra). Explain why this event qualifies as mutawatir according to Ibn Taymiyya's criteria, and contrast it with a philosophical claim like 'the world is eternal'. Which has stronger tawatur and why?
?
Find another example of a widely known historical event from Islamic history (e.g., the Battle of Badr) and assess its tawatur level using the principles from this passage.

Prophetic Tawatur Surpasses Philosophical Tawatur
Comparison of prophetic and philosophical tawatur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the epistemological strength of tawatur in prophetic reports versus philosophical claims, using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria.

Core Idea
Prophetic tawatur is indisputable, philosophical tawatur is not.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya directly challenges the philosophers' dismissal of prophetic tawatur as a source of certain knowledge. He argues that the widespread transmission of prophetic events is far greater and more reliable than any philosophical claim, and he uses historical dating as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim
Find where Ibn Taymiyya says that 'some of their devils' claim that tawatur does not establish demonstrative proof (burhan) against an opponent. This is the starting point of his refutation.
The philosophers aim to exclude prophetic reports from being considered burhan.
2
Find Ibn Taymiyya's counter-claim
Locate his assertion that the tawatur of Muhammad's emergence and the Qur'an is greater than that of all philosophers, and that reports of Moses and Jesus are similarly superior.
3
Examine the dating evidence
Notice how he uses the fact that prophetic events are used for dating calendars (e.g., Hijra calendar, Roman calendar after Alexander) to show their widespread knowledge and acceptance among people.
This empirical observation supports his argument.
4
Compare tawatur levels
Contrast the widespread knowledge of prophets with the obscure origins of philosophers like Aristotle, known only through his association with Alexander or through books with limited transmission.
Philosophers are known through books, not through universal tawatur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الثامن : المتواتر عن الأنبياء أعظم من المتواتر عن الفلاسفة

فنقول : معلوم أن من شياطينهم من يقول : المتواترات لا يقوم بها البرهان على المنازع ليُدْخِل في ذلك ما تواتر عن الأنبياء - صلوات الله عليهم - من الآيات والبراهين، والمعجزات، التي بعثوا بها، كما يُدخلون ما أُخِذ عن الأنبياء من المقبولات .

فيقال لهم : من المعلوم بالاضطرار أن تواثر خروج محمد ـ صلى الله عليه وسلم - ومجيئه بهذا القرآن أعظم عند أهل الأرض من تواتر وجود الفلاسفة كلهم، فضلاً عما يُخبرون به من القضايا التجربية والحدسية التي استدلوا بها على الطبيعيات والفلكيات . وكذلك ما تواتر من سائر معجزاته وما تواتر من أخبار موسى والمسيح - صلوات الله عليهما. هذا معلوم عند الناس أعظم من تواتر وجود أولئك فضلاً عن تَوَاتُر ما يخبرون به .

ولهذا صار ظهور الأنبياء مما تؤرّخ به الحوادث في العالم لظهور أمرهم عند الخاصة والعامة. فإن التأريخ يكون بالحادث المشهور الذي يشترك الناس فيه ليعرفوا به كم مضى بعده، وقبله كما أن النهار يعرف بطلوع الشمس والشهر بالهلال، لأنه نور ظاهر يشترك الناس في رؤيته . ولهذا جعل عمرُ تأريخ المسلمين من الهجرة النبوية، فإنها أظهرُ أحوال الرسول المشهورة، وهو خروجه من بلد إلى بلد، وبها أعزّ الله الإسلام. وكانت العرب قبل الإسلام تؤرّخ بالحوادث المشهورة، وكذلك الروم، والفرس والقِبْط، وسائر الأمم، يؤرخون مثل ذلك فنحن اليوم إذا أردنا أن نعرف زمان واحد من هؤلاء المتفلسفة قلنا كان قبل المسيح بكذا وكذا سنة . بل أرسطو إنما عُرف زمانه لأنه قد عرف أنه كان وزير الإسكندر بن فيلبس المقدوني، ملك اليونان. وكانوا مشركين يعبدون الكواكب والأصنام، ويُعانون السحر - أرسطو وملكه وغيرهما. وهذا الإسكندر لما جاء إلى الشام أيام بني إسرائيل غَلَب عليهم. فذكروا أنه طلب أن يُكتب في التوراة فقالوا: «ما يمكن هذا»، فقال: اجعلوا لي تأريخاً»، فصار التأريخ الرومي الذي تؤرّخ به اليهود والنصارى مؤرخاً به .

وأرسطو وزيره، فعُرف وقته من هذا الوجه. وكان قبل المسيح بثلاث مئة سنة . والتواريخ التي تختص بها اليهود هي من الأنبياء وأحوال بيت المقدس — يقولون: «في البيت الأول»، «في البيت الثاني».

ثم عرف أرسطو بهذه الكتب المنسوبة إليه، كما عُرف بطلميوس بـ «المجسطي» وكما عرف أبقراط وجالينوس بما ينسب إليهما من كتب الطب. وإلا، فأي شيء لم تتواتر هو الذي تواتر عند الناس من أخبار هؤلاء، فضلاً عن أن يتواتر عنهم ما يذكرونه في كتبهم من القضايا التجربية والحدسية. وغاية ما يوجد أن يقول بطلميوس هذا مما رصده فلان»، وأن يقول جالينوس : هذا مما جرّبته أنا» أو «ذكر لي فلان أنه جربه» أو نحو ذلك من الحكايات التي ملأ بها جالينوس كتابه وليس في هذه شيء من المتواتر. وإن قدّر أن غيره جرب أيضاً فذاك خبر واحد .

ولكن ما يدعى في تجارب الأطباء من الأدوية أقرب إلى التسليم مما يدعونه في تجاربهم الرَّصدية. وذلك لاشتراك كثير من الأطباء في تجربة الدواء الواحد. وأيضاً، فلكثرة وجود ما يُدَّعى فيه التجربة من النبات وتواطؤ المجرّبين له. وليس كذلك ما يدعونه من فلسفتهم فإنا رأينا تجارب الأطباء على غير مِنوالهم، وعلمنا صدقها كثيراً. وليس القصد إلا الإعلام بفساد تأصيلهم فقط وإلا، فالأطباء في تجاربهم أسد حالاً من الفلسفة
The Fourth Station - The Eighth Aspect: The widely transmitted reports about the prophets are greater than the widely transmitted reports about the philosophers.

We say: It is known that some of their devils say: 'Demonstrative proof is not established by widely transmitted reports against the opponent,' so that they may include in that what has been transmitted widely from the prophets—peace be upon them—of signs, proofs, and miracles with which they were sent, just as they include what has been taken from the prophets of accepted opinions.

So it is said to them: It is known necessarily that the widespread transmission of the emergence of Muhammad—peace be upon him—and his coming with this Qur'an is greater among the people of the earth than the widespread transmission of the existence of all philosophers, let alone what they report of empirical and intuitive propositions by which they argue for natural and astronomical phenomena. Likewise, what has been widely transmitted of his other miracles and what has been widely transmitted of the reports of Moses and the Messiah—peace be upon them—this is known among people as greater than the widespread transmission of the existence of those individuals, let alone the widespread transmission of what they report.

For this reason, the appearance of the prophets became something by which events in the world are dated, due to the prominence of their affair among the elite and the common people. Dating is by a well-known event that people share in order to know how much time has passed after it and before it, just as the day is known by the rising of the sun and the month by the crescent, because it is a manifest light that people share in seeing. For this reason, Umar established the dating of the Muslims from the prophetic migration, for it is the most prominent of the Prophet's well-known states—his departure from one city to another—and through it God strengthened Islam. The Arabs before Islam used to date by well-known events, and likewise the Romans, Persians, Copts, and other nations date by similar things. Today, if we want to know the time of one of these philosophers, we say: he was so many years before Christ. Rather, Aristotle's time is known only because it is known that he was the vizier of Alexander son of Philip of Macedon, king of the Greeks. They were polytheists worshipping planets and idols, and practicing magic—Aristotle, his king, and others. This Alexander, when he came to Syria in the days of the Children of Israel, overcame them. They mentioned that he asked to have his name written in the Torah, but they said: 'This is not possible.' He said: 'Make a dating for me,' so the Roman dating appeared, by which the Jews and Christians date.

Aristotle, his vizier, was known for his time from this aspect. He was three hundred years before Christ. The histories specific to the Jews are from the prophets and the conditions of the Temple—they say: 'In the First Temple,' 'In the Second Temple.'

Then Aristotle was known through these books attributed to him, just as Ptolemy was known through the 'Almagest' and as Hippocrates and Galen were known through what is attributed to them of medical books. Otherwise, what has not been widely transmitted is that which has been widely transmitted among people of the reports of these individuals, let alone that what they mention in their books of empirical and intuitive propositions should be widely transmitted. The utmost found is that Ptolemy says: 'This is from the observation of so-and-so,' and that Galen says: 'This is something I have experimented' or 'so-and-so told me that he experimented' or the like of such anecdotes with which Galen filled his book. There is nothing in this of widespread transmission. Even if it is supposed that someone else also experimented, that is a solitary report.

However, what is claimed in the experiments of physicians regarding medicines is closer to acceptance than what they claim in their observational experiments. That is because many physicians share in experimenting with a single drug, and also because of the abundance of what is claimed to have been experimented with from plants and the concurrence of experimenters. It is not so with what they claim in their philosophy, for we have seen the experiments of physicians not following their pattern, and we have known their truthfulness frequently. The aim is only to inform of the corruption of their foundational principles; otherwise, physicians in their experiments are in a better state than the philosophers.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This is a critical passage where Ibn Taymiyya refutes the philosopher's claim that widely transmitted reports (tawatur) cannot serve as demonstrative proof. He demonstrates that the tawatur of prophetic events is far greater and more certain than any philosophical claim.

Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that some devils among the philosophers argue that tawatur does not constitute a proof against the opponent, thereby dismissing the reports of prophets' miracles and signs. In response, he asserts that the tawatur of Muhammad's emergence and the coming of the Quran is greater among the people of the earth than the tawatur of all philosophers, let alone their empirical and intuitive propositions about natural and astronomical matters. Similarly, the tawatur of other miracles of Muhammad and of Moses and Jesus is greater than the tawatur of the philosophers' existence.

He then draws attention to how the appearance of prophets is used as a basis for dating events worldwide, indicating the widespread recognition of their significance. Dating relies on well-known events shared by people, just as the day is known by the sunrise and the month by the crescent moon. He references Umar's adoption of the Hijra calendar as an example, and mentions that various nations date by major events. In contrast, the knowledge of philosophers like Aristotle is derived from his association with Alexander, a historical figure of uncertain reliability.

Ibn Taymiyya critiques the empirical claims of philosophers, arguing that they lack tawatur. Ptolemy references individual observations, and Galen's anecdotes are based on solitary experiments. Even if others repeated the experiment, it remains a solitary report. In contrast, the tawatur of prophetic reports is widespread and indisputable.

Finally, he distinguishes between medical experiments and philosophical experiments. Medical experiments are more reliable because many physicians share in testing a single drug, and there is abundant concurrence. Philosophical claims lack such widespread confirmation. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that physicians are in a better state than philosophers, and his aim is to expose the corruption of the philosophers' foundational principles.

برهان

Key Takeaway
Prophetic tawatur provides a level of certainty that philosophical reports cannot match, as evidenced by its use in dating world events.

Critique of Philosophical Empiricism: Lack of Tawatur
Critique of philosophical empirical claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's critique of philosophical empirical claims as lacking tawatur and distinguish them from more reliable medical experiments.

Core Idea
Philosophical 'experiments' are solitary reports, not widespread transmission.

Ibn Taymiyya turns his attention to the empirical and intuitive propositions that philosophers claim as certain knowledge. He scrutinizes the transmission of these claims, revealing that they are based on individual observations or anecdotes, not on the widespread transmission that yields certainty. He also contrasts this with medical experiments, which are more reliable due to shared experimentation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of claims philosophers make
Locate where Ibn Taymiyya mentions 'empirical and intuitive propositions' (al-qadaya al-tajribiyya wa al-hadsiyya) used for natural and astronomical matters.
These are the claims philosophers rely on for their sciences.
2
Examine how these claims are transmitted
Find where he describes Ptolemy's transmission ('this is from the observation of so-and-so') and Galen's anecdotes ('this is something I have experimented' or 'so-and-so told me'). Note that these are solitary reports, not widely transmitted.
Even if someone else repeated the experiment, it remains a khabar wahid (solitary report).
3
Note his conclusion on tawatur
Identify his statement: 'There is nothing in this of widespread transmission.' He emphasizes that philosophical claims lack the tawatur required for certainty.
4
Contrast with medical experiments
See how medical experiments are closer to acceptance because many physicians share in testing a single drug, leading to concurrence. This makes them more reliable than philosophical experiments.
5
Extract his overall aim
Understand that his aim is not to dismiss all empirical knowledge but to expose the 'corruption of their foundational principles' – the philosophers' unjustified claim to certainty.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الثامن : المتواتر عن الأنبياء أعظم من المتواتر عن الفلاسفة

فنقول : معلوم أن من شياطينهم من يقول : المتواترات لا يقوم بها البرهان على المنازع ليُدْخِل في ذلك ما تواتر عن الأنبياء - صلوات الله عليهم - من الآيات والبراهين، والمعجزات، التي بعثوا بها، كما يُدخلون ما أُخِذ عن الأنبياء من المقبولات .

فيقال لهم : من المعلوم بالاضطرار أن تواثر خروج محمد ـ صلى الله عليه وسلم - ومجيئه بهذا القرآن أعظم عند أهل الأرض من تواتر وجود الفلاسفة كلهم، فضلاً عما يُخبرون به من القضايا التجربية والحدسية التي استدلوا بها على الطبيعيات والفلكيات . وكذلك ما تواتر من سائر معجزاته وما تواتر من أخبار موسى والمسيح - صلوات الله عليهما. هذا معلوم عند الناس أعظم من تواتر وجود أولئك فضلاً عن تَوَاتُر ما يخبرون به .

ولهذا صار ظهور الأنبياء مما تؤرّخ به الحوادث في العالم لظهور أمرهم عند الخاصة والعامة. فإن التأريخ يكون بالحادث المشهور الذي يشترك الناس فيه ليعرفوا به كم مضى بعده، وقبله كما أن النهار يعرف بطلوع الشمس والشهر بالهلال، لأنه نور ظاهر يشترك الناس في رؤيته . ولهذا جعل عمرُ تأريخ المسلمين من الهجرة النبوية، فإنها أظهرُ أحوال الرسول المشهورة، وهو خروجه من بلد إلى بلد، وبها أعزّ الله الإسلام. وكانت العرب قبل الإسلام تؤرّخ بالحوادث المشهورة، وكذلك الروم، والفرس والقِبْط، وسائر الأمم، يؤرخون مثل ذلك فنحن اليوم إذا أردنا أن نعرف زمان واحد من هؤلاء المتفلسفة قلنا كان قبل المسيح بكذا وكذا سنة . بل أرسطو إنما عُرف زمانه لأنه قد عرف أنه كان وزير الإسكندر بن فيلبس المقدوني، ملك اليونان. وكانوا مشركين يعبدون الكواكب والأصنام، ويُعانون السحر - أرسطو وملكه وغيرهما. وهذا الإسكندر لما جاء إلى الشام أيام بني إسرائيل غَلَب عليهم. فذكروا أنه طلب أن يُكتب في التوراة فقالوا: «ما يمكن هذا»، فقال: اجعلوا لي تأريخاً»، فصار التأريخ الرومي الذي تؤرّخ به اليهود والنصارى مؤرخاً به .

وأرسطو وزيره، فعُرف وقته من هذا الوجه. وكان قبل المسيح بثلاث مئة سنة . والتواريخ التي تختص بها اليهود هي من الأنبياء وأحوال بيت المقدس — يقولون: «في البيت الأول»، «في البيت الثاني».

ثم عرف أرسطو بهذه الكتب المنسوبة إليه، كما عُرف بطلميوس بـ «المجسطي» وكما عرف أبقراط وجالينوس بما ينسب إليهما من كتب الطب. وإلا، فأي شيء لم تتواتر هو الذي تواتر عند الناس من أخبار هؤلاء، فضلاً عن أن يتواتر عنهم ما يذكرونه في كتبهم من القضايا التجربية والحدسية. وغاية ما يوجد أن يقول بطلميوس هذا مما رصده فلان»، وأن يقول جالينوس : هذا مما جرّبته أنا» أو «ذكر لي فلان أنه جربه» أو نحو ذلك من الحكايات التي ملأ بها جالينوس كتابه وليس في هذه شيء من المتواتر. وإن قدّر أن غيره جرب أيضاً فذاك خبر واحد .

ولكن ما يدعى في تجارب الأطباء من الأدوية أقرب إلى التسليم مما يدعونه في تجاربهم الرَّصدية. وذلك لاشتراك كثير من الأطباء في تجربة الدواء الواحد. وأيضاً، فلكثرة وجود ما يُدَّعى فيه التجربة من النبات وتواطؤ المجرّبين له. وليس كذلك ما يدعونه من فلسفتهم فإنا رأينا تجارب الأطباء على غير مِنوالهم، وعلمنا صدقها كثيراً. وليس القصد إلا الإعلام بفساد تأصيلهم فقط وإلا، فالأطباء في تجاربهم أسد حالاً من الفلسفة
The Fourth Station - The Eighth Aspect: The widely transmitted reports about the prophets are greater than the widely transmitted reports about the philosophers.

We say: It is known that some of their devils say: 'Demonstrative proof is not established by widely transmitted reports against the opponent,' so that they may include in that what has been transmitted widely from the prophets—peace be upon them—of signs, proofs, and miracles with which they were sent, just as they include what has been taken from the prophets of accepted opinions.

So it is said to them: It is known necessarily that the widespread transmission of the emergence of Muhammad—peace be upon him—and his coming with this Qur'an is greater among the people of the earth than the widespread transmission of the existence of all philosophers, let alone what they report of empirical and intuitive propositions by which they argue for natural and astronomical phenomena. Likewise, what has been widely transmitted of his other miracles and what has been widely transmitted of the reports of Moses and the Messiah—peace be upon them—this is known among people as greater than the widespread transmission of the existence of those individuals, let alone the widespread transmission of what they report.

For this reason, the appearance of the prophets became something by which events in the world are dated, due to the prominence of their affair among the elite and the common people. Dating is by a well-known event that people share in order to know how much time has passed after it and before it, just as the day is known by the rising of the sun and the month by the crescent, because it is a manifest light that people share in seeing. For this reason, Umar established the dating of the Muslims from the prophetic migration, for it is the most prominent of the Prophet's well-known states—his departure from one city to another—and through it God strengthened Islam. The Arabs before Islam used to date by well-known events, and likewise the Romans, Persians, Copts, and other nations date by similar things. Today, if we want to know the time of one of these philosophers, we say: he was so many years before Christ. Rather, Aristotle's time is known only because it is known that he was the vizier of Alexander son of Philip of Macedon, king of the Greeks. They were polytheists worshipping planets and idols, and practicing magic—Aristotle, his king, and others. This Alexander, when he came to Syria in the days of the Children of Israel, overcame them. They mentioned that he asked to have his name written in the Torah, but they said: 'This is not possible.' He said: 'Make a dating for me,' so the Roman dating appeared, by which the Jews and Christians date.

Aristotle, his vizier, was known for his time from this aspect. He was three hundred years before Christ. The histories specific to the Jews are from the prophets and the conditions of the Temple—they say: 'In the First Temple,' 'In the Second Temple.'

Then Aristotle was known through these books attributed to him, just as Ptolemy was known through the 'Almagest' and as Hippocrates and Galen were known through what is attributed to them of medical books. Otherwise, what has not been widely transmitted is that which has been widely transmitted among people of the reports of these individuals, let alone that what they mention in their books of empirical and intuitive propositions should be widely transmitted. The utmost found is that Ptolemy says: 'This is from the observation of so-and-so,' and that Galen says: 'This is something I have experimented' or 'so-and-so told me that he experimented' or the like of such anecdotes with which Galen filled his book. There is nothing in this of widespread transmission. Even if it is supposed that someone else also experimented, that is a solitary report.

However, what is claimed in the experiments of physicians regarding medicines is closer to acceptance than what they claim in their observational experiments. That is because many physicians share in experimenting with a single drug, and also because of the abundance of what is claimed to have been experimented with from plants and the concurrence of experimenters. It is not so with what they claim in their philosophy, for we have seen the experiments of physicians not following their pattern, and we have known their truthfulness frequently. The aim is only to inform of the corruption of their foundational principles; otherwise, physicians in their experiments are in a better state than the philosophers.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This is a critical passage where Ibn Taymiyya refutes the philosopher's claim that widely transmitted reports (tawatur) cannot serve as demonstrative proof. He demonstrates that the tawatur of prophetic events is far greater and more certain than any philosophical claim.

Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that some devils among the philosophers argue that tawatur does not constitute a proof against the opponent, thereby dismissing the reports of prophets' miracles and signs. In response, he asserts that the tawatur of Muhammad's emergence and the coming of the Quran is greater among the people of the earth than the tawatur of all philosophers, let alone their empirical and intuitive propositions about natural and astronomical matters. Similarly, the tawatur of other miracles of Muhammad and of Moses and Jesus is greater than the tawatur of the philosophers' existence.

He then draws attention to how the appearance of prophets is used as a basis for dating events worldwide, indicating the widespread recognition of their significance. Dating relies on well-known events shared by people, just as the day is known by the sunrise and the month by the crescent moon. He references Umar's adoption of the Hijra calendar as an example, and mentions that various nations date by major events. In contrast, the knowledge of philosophers like Aristotle is derived from his association with Alexander, a historical figure of uncertain reliability.

Ibn Taymiyya critiques the empirical claims of philosophers, arguing that they lack tawatur. Ptolemy references individual observations, and Galen's anecdotes are based on solitary experiments. Even if others repeated the experiment, it remains a solitary report. In contrast, the tawatur of prophetic reports is widespread and indisputable.

Finally, he distinguishes between medical experiments and philosophical experiments. Medical experiments are more reliable because many physicians share in testing a single drug, and there is abundant concurrence. Philosophical claims lack such widespread confirmation. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that physicians are in a better state than philosophers, and his aim is to expose the corruption of the philosophers' foundational principles.

Key Terms
قضايا تجربية
قضايا حدسية
متواتر
خبر واحد

Why does Ibn Taymiyya consider medical experiments more reliable than philosophical experiments?
A) They are based on intuition
B) Many physicians share in testing a single drug
C) They are written in books
D) They are ancient

Key Takeaway
For empirical knowledge to be certain, it must be transmitted widely; philosophical claims fail this test, while medical experiments often succeed due to shared practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Philosophical Tawatur
Ibn Taymiyya contrasts prophetic and philosophical tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that prophetic tawatur is epistemically superior to philosophical reports, and evaluate its implications for the certainty of metaphysical claims.

Core Idea
Prophetic tawatur yields certainty; philosophical tawatur is an illusion.

In this passage from his Refutation of the Logicians, Ibn Taymiyya challenges the philosophers' claim that their empirical and astronomical knowledge is established through tawatur (massive, certain transmission). He argues that their reports are actually isolated (khabar wahid) and do not reach the level of mutawatir, while the prophetic traditions are genuinely mutawatir. This critique undermines the philosophers' confidence in their rational demonstrations, especially in metaphysics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two kinds of tawatur compared
Ibn Taymiyya contrasts the mutawatir from the prophets with the putative mutawatir from philosophers like Aristotle, Ptolemy, and Galen. The former is claimed to be genuine, the latter is questioned.
The passage begins by asserting that prophetic mutawatir is greater.
2
Deconstruct the philosophers' claim to tawatur
He examines how Ptolemy and Galen transmit their observations: individual reports, often based on personal experiment or hearsay, not widespread independent chains.
These are classified as khabar wahid, not mutawatir.
3
Analyze the medical analogy
Medical experiments are more reliable than philosophical claims because many physicians share experiments on the same drug, yet even those are not truly mutawatir.
This shows the philosophers' claims are even weaker.
4
Trace the final argument
If someone denies demonstration from prophetic tawatur, they cannot rely on philosophical tawatur for demonstration. Moreover, Aristotle's theology is deeply ignorant, showing the inferiority of philosophical knowledge.
Ibn Taymiyya uses analogy: equating philosophy with prophecy is like equating village chiefs with kings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الثامن : المتواتر عن الأنبياء أعظم من المتواتر عن الفلاسفة وأرسطو وزيره، فعُرف وقته من هذا الوجه. وكان قبل المسيح بثلاث مئة سنة . والتواريخ التي تختص بها اليهود هي من الأنبياء وأحوال بيت المقدس ـ يقولون: «في البيت الأول»، «في البيت الثاني». ثم عرف أرسطو بهذه الكتب المنسوبة إليه، كما عُرف بطلميوس بـ «المجسطي) وكما عرف أبقراط وجالينوس بما ينسب إليهما من كتب الطب. وإلا، فأي شيء لم تتواتر هو الذي تواتر عند الناس من أخبار هؤلاء، فضلاً عن أن يتواتر عنهم ما يذكرونه في كتبهم من القضايا التجربية والحدسية. وغاية ما يوجد أن يقول بطلميوس هذا مما رصده فلان»، وأن يقول جالينوس: هذا مما جرّبته أنا» أو «ذكر لي فلان أنه جربه» أو نحو ذلك من الحكايات التي ملأ بها جالينوس كتابه وليس في هذه شيء من المتواتر. وإن قدّر أن غيره جرب أيضاً فذاك خبر واحد . ولكن ما يدعى في تجارب الأطباء من الأدوية أقرب إلى التسليم مما يدعونه في تجارب الأطباء أسد تجاربهم الرَّصدية. وذلك لاشتراك كثير من الأطباء في تجربة الدواء الواحد. وأيضاً، فلكثرة وجود ما يُدَّعى فيه التجربة من النبات وتواطؤ المجرّبين له. وليس كذلك ما يدعونه من فلسفتهم فإنا رأينا تجارب الأطباء على غير مِنوالهم، وعلمنا صدقها كثيراً. وليس القصد إلا الإعلام بفساد تأصيلهم فقط وإلا، فالأطباء في تجاربهم أسد حالاً من الفلسفة. منهم، كتاب الرد على المنطقيين لأن القوم إنما يذكرون دواء موجوداً يمكن تجربته كثيراً لوجوده، ولكثرة المحتاجين إليه ممن يصيبه ما يقال إن ذلك الدواء يؤثر فيه شفاء، والله فاعل ذلك الشفاء ذلك الدواء. فبينهم حينئذ فرق من حيث ما قررته . فالتواتر عزيز عندهم جداً. وأكثر الناس لم يجربوا جميع ما جربوه، ولا علموا أكثر تجاربهم بالأرصاد ما ادعوا أنهم علموه. وإذا قيل: «قد اتفق على ذلك رَصْدُ فلان وفلان» كان غاية ما عندهم أن يذكروا جماعة رصدوا . وهذا غايته أن يكون من التواتر الخاص الذي خبر واحد أو طائفة لا يعرف الفلاسفة ما ينقله طائفة . فمن زعم أنه لا يقوم عليه برهان بما تواتر عن الأنبياء كيف يمكنه أن يقيم على غيره برهاناً بمثل هذا التواتر ويعظم علم الهيئة والفلسفة، ويدعي أنه علم عقلي معلوم بالبرهان؟ وهذا أعظم ما يقوم عليه البرهان العقلي عندهم هذا حاله! فما الظن بالإلهيات التي إذا نظر فيها كلام معلّمهم الأول - أرسطو - أو تدبَّره الفاضل العاقل لم يفده إلا العلم بأنهم كانوا من أجهل الخلق برب العالمين؟ وصار يتعجب تعجباً لا ينقضي ممن يقرن علم هؤلاء بالإلهيات إلى ما جاءت به الأنبياء، ويرى أن هذا من جنس من يقرن الحدادين بالملائكة، بل من يقرن دَهَاقينَ القرى بملوك العالم، فهو أقرب إلى العلم والعدل ممن يقرن هؤلاء بالأنبياء، فإن دهقان القرية متولّ عليها كتولي الملك على مملكته، فله جُزء من الملك . وأما ما جاءت به الأنبياء فلا يعرفه هؤلاء ألبتة وليسوا قريبين منه . بل كفّارُ اليهود والنصارى أعلم منهم بالأمور الإلهية. ولست أعني بذلك ما اختَصَّ الأنبياء بينه الرسل بالأدلة العقلية بعلمه من الوحي الذي لا يناله غيرهم، فإن هذا ليس من علمهم ولا من علم غيرهم . وإنما أعني العلوم العقلية التي بينها الرسلُ للناس بالبراهين العقلية في أمر معرفة الرب، وتوحيده، ومعرفة أسمائه وصفاته وفي النبوات والمعاد وما جاءوا به من مصالح
The fourth station - the eighth aspect: The mutawatir from the prophets is greater than the mutawatir from the philosophers. And Aristotle was his vizier, so his time was known from this aspect. And he was three hundred years before Christ. And the histories that are specific to the Jews are from the prophets and the states of the Temple — they say: 'in the first Temple', 'in the second Temple'. Then Aristotle became known through these books attributed to him, just as Ptolemy became known through Almagest, and just as Hippocrates and Galen became known through what is attributed to them of medical books. Otherwise, is there anything that is not mutawatir that is mutawatir among people from the reports of these? Much less that what they mention in their books of experiential and intuitive propositions is mutawatir from them. The utmost found is that Ptolemy says: 'this is from what so-and-so observed', and Galen says: 'this is from what I myself experimented' or 'so-and-so told me that he experimented' or the like of such stories with which Galen filled his book, and there is nothing of mutawatir in these. And if it is assumed that someone else also experimented, then that is a khabar wahid. But what is claimed in the experiments of physicians concerning medicines is closer to acceptance than what they claim in their experiments — the physicians are more correct in their observational experiments. That is because many physicians share in experimenting on one medicine. Also, due to the abundance of what is claimed to be experimented upon from plants and the agreement of the experimenters upon it. And it is not like what they claim from their philosophy, for we have seen the experiments of physicians not on their pattern, and we have known their truth often. And the intent is only to inform of the corruption of their principles only; otherwise, the physicians in their experiments are in a better state than the philosophers. Among them, the Book of Refutation of the Logicians, because the people only mention an existing medicine that can be experimented upon frequently due to its existence, and due to the many needy ones among those whom it is said that this medicine affects healing, and Allah is the doer of that healing through that medicine. So between them then is a difference from what I established. So tawatur is rare among them greatly. And most people have not experimented all that they have experimented, nor do they know most of their experiments through observations that they claimed to know. And if it is said: 'such and such and such and such have agreed on that observation', the utmost they have is to mention a group who observed. And this at most is from the private tawatur that is a khabar wahid or a group — the philosophers do not know what a group transmits. So whoever claims that no demonstration is established for him through what is mutawatir from the prophets, how can he establish a demonstration for others through this kind of tawatur, and magnify the science of astronomy and philosophy, and claim that it is a rational science known through demonstration? And this is the greatest demonstration of rational proof according to them — this is its state! So what is the opinion about the divine matters that when one looks at the speech of their first teacher — Aristotle — or the virtuous intelligent person contemplates it, it gives him nothing but the knowledge that they were among the most ignorant of creation concerning the Lord of the worlds. And he becomes amazed with endless amazement at one who equates the knowledge of these with divine matters to what the prophets brought, and sees that this is like one who equates blacksmiths with angels, rather like one who equates village chiefs with the kings of the world, for he is closer to knowledge and justice than one who equates these with the prophets. For the village chief is in charge of the village like the king's charge over his kingdom, so he has a portion of kingship. And as for what the prophets brought, these do not know it at all and are not near it. Rather, the disbelievers among the Jews and Christians are more knowledgeable than them about divine matters. And I do not mean by that what is specific to the prophets — what the messengers revealed of revelation that no one else attains, for that is not from their knowledge nor from the knowledge of others. Rather, I mean the rational sciences that the messengers expounded to people through rational demonstrations concerning the knowledge of the Lord, His oneness, the knowledge of His names and attributes, prophethood, the return, and the benefits they brought.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument from Ibn Taymiyya against the logicians' claim that philosophical and empirical knowledge is established through tawatur (massive transmission yielding certainty) while rejecting the tawatur of prophetic traditions. He begins by asserting that mutawatir reports from the prophets are greater than those from philosophers, using the example of Aristotle known through his writings and historical context. He then contrasts the transmission of astronomical and medical knowledge: Ptolemy's observations and Galen's experiments are based on isolated reports (khabar wahid) rather than tawatur. He acknowledges that medical experiments are more reliable because many physicians share experiences on the same medicine, but the specifics of each experiment remain individual reports. In contrast, philosophical claims lack even this level of corroboration. Ibn Taymiyya then argues that tawatur is rare among philosophers; their utmost is citing a group of observers, which constitutes at most a 'private tawatur' equivalent to a single report. He concludes that if someone denies demonstration based on prophetic tawatur, they cannot establish demonstration based on their own weak tawatur. Finally, he sharply criticizes Aristotle's theology, stating that studying his works reveals his ignorance of God, and compares equating philosophy with prophetic knowledge to equating blacksmiths with angels or village chiefs with kings. The passage guards against the misconception that philosophical or scientific consensus achieves the same certainty as prophetic tawatur.

Key Terms
المتواتر
الخبر الواحد
التجربة
البرهان
الإلهيات

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in the passage, what is the epistemic status of most philosophical claims about astronomy and medicine?
A) They are mutawatir because many scholars agree.
B) They are khabar wahid, not mutawatir.
C) They are burhan (demonstration) without need for tawatur.
D) They are more reliable than prophetic reports.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic tawatur is epistemically superior to philosophical reports; the latter are at best khabar wahid and cannot ground certain demonstrations in theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Compare the transmission of a medical report (e.g., the effectiveness of honey as a cure) with the transmission of a hadith about honey's healing properties. How does each achieve tawatur or not, according to Ibn Taymiyya's criteria?
?
2. Evaluate a claim from a modern science textbook: is the fact that 'water boils at 100°C' mutawatir in Ibn Taymiyya's sense? What about the Darwinian theory of evolution? Discuss the epistemological differences.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of the Logicians' Distinction Between First Principles and Common Notions
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the logicians' distinction is based on a false ontology and is epistemologically relative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the logicians' distinction between awwaliyat and mashhurat is based on a false ontology and is epistemologically relative.

Core Idea
The distinction is not a fixed genus but a relative judgment depending on the knower.

Ibn Taymiyya attacks the very foundation of the logicians' classification. He argues that their claim that some necessary attributes require a real middle term is false, and that the distinction between self-evident and non-self-evident is merely epistemological, varying from person to person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' claim
State the distinction: first principles (awwaliyat) are those where the subject is affirmed to the predicate without needing a middle term in both mental and external existence; otherwise they are not first principles.
This claim implies an ontological difference: some necessary attributes have a real middle term.
2
Analyze Ibn Sina's interpretation
Ibn Taymiyya notes that Ibn Sina interpreted 'middle term' as the mental proof (dalil) in a syllogism, not an ontological link. This suggests that the distinction is epistemic, not ontological.
3
Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of the ontology
He asserts that all necessary attributes are directly necessary to their subject; there is no real middle term in reality. The necessity is immediate, whether known or not.
Examples: inferring cause from effect, etc., show the proof is mental.
4
Extract the epistemological argument
Self-evidence is a relation between the knower and the known, not an intrinsic property. It varies with people's knowledge and mental capacity. Therefore, the distinction does not divide propositions into fixed genera.
5
Evaluate the overall critique
Assess: Ibn Taymiyya undermines the objective basis of the logicians' classification, reducing it to a subjective judgment. The critique is valid if one accepts that necessity is direct and knowledge is relative.

النوع الأول : إن التفريق بين الأوليات وغيرها بأن الأوليات ما كان ثبوت الموضوع للمحمول وهو ثبوت الصفة للموصوف والمحكوم به للمحكوم عليه والمخبر به للمخبر عنه كثبوت الخبر للمبتدأ بالتفريق بين «الأولي» وغيره بأن الموضوع إن ثبت للمحمول بنفسه في الوجودين - الذهني والخارجي - فهو أولي، وإن افتقر إلى وسط فليس بأولي، فرق فاسد مبني على أصل فاسد وهو أن الصفات اللازمة للموصوف، منها ما يلزم بنفسه ليس بينه وبين الموصوف وسط في نفس الأمر، ومنها ما لا يلزم بنفسه بل بوسط في نفس الأمر يكون ذلك الوسط لازماً للموصوف ويكون هذا المحمول لازماً لذلك اللازم. وهذا الفرق قد ذكره غير واحد كالرازي وغيره في الصفات اللازمة. وابن سينا ذكره أيضاً، لكن ابن سينا ذكر أنه إنما أراد بـ «الوسط» «الحد الأوسط في القياس»، وهو ما يُقرن باللام في قولك لأنه». وهذا هو الدليل، والدليل هو وسط في الذهن للمستدل، ليس هو وسطاً في نفس ثبوت الصفة للموصوف فإنه قد يستدل بالمعلول على العلة، كما يستدل بالعلة على المعلول، ويستدل بأحد المعلولين على الآخر، ويستدل بثبوت أحد الضدين على انتفاء الآخر، وبثبوت أحد المتلازمين على تحقق الآخر. ولا ريب أن الصفات اللازمة للموصوف تنقسم إلى ما لزومه بين للإنسان، وإلى ما ليس هو بيناً بل يفتقر ملزومه إلى دليل. وكونه بيناً للإنسان وغير بين ليس هو الشيء في نفسه، وإنما هو إخبار عن علم الإنسان به وتنبيه له. فهو إخبار عن الوجود الذهني، لا الخارجي، فما كان بيناً للإنسان معلوماً له موجوداً في ذهنه لم يحتج فيه إلى دليل . وما لم يكن كذلك احتاج فيه إلى دليل، وكون الشيء بيناً وغير بين نسبة وإضافة بين المعلوم والإنسان العالم. وهذا تختلف فيه أحوال الناس، فقد يتبين لزيد ما لا يتبين لعمرو . فإن أسباب العلم وقوة الشعور وجودة الأذهان متفاوتة. فلا يلزم إذا تبين لإنسان ثبوت بعض الصفات أو لزومها أو اتصاف الموصوف بها أن يتبين ذلك لكل أحد، ولا يلزم إذا خفي على بعض الناس أن يكون خفياً على كل أحد. وحينئذ، فإذا فرق بين الأولي وغيره بأن الأولي ما لا يحتاج إلى وسط، فكون القضية أولية أو غير أولية فرق إضافي بحسب أحوال الناس . فيكون ذلك بمنزلة أن يقال : القضية إما أن تكون معلومة وإما أن لا تكون وإما أن تكون ظاهرة وإما أن لا تكون، وإما أن تكون واضحة وإما أن لا تكون وإما أن تكون جلية وإما أن لا تكون وإما أن يتصور الإنسان صدقها وإما أن لا يتصور. وهذا فرق صحيح، فإن كل قضية بالنسبة إلى كل أحد إما أن تكون بينة له وإما أن لا تكون بينة له . لكن ليس هذا الفرق يميز بين أجناس القضايا حتى يجعل جنس منها بتمامه من قبيل غير البين وجنس آخر بتمامه من جنس البين . فإن هذا الفرق لا يعود إلى صفة لازمة للقضية كما ادعاه من أن اللازم البين ما ثبت للموصوف بلا وسط في نفس الأمر، واللازم غير البين ما كان ثبوته بوسط في نفس الأمر. بل جميع اللوازم للموصوف ليس بينها وبين الموصوف وسط أصلاً في نفس الأمر. وإن احتاج الإنسان في علمه بثبوتها إلى دليل فليس كل ما لا يعلم لزومه للموصوف إلا بدليل لا يكون ثبوته له إلا بوسط، كما تقدم بيانه. فإن المعلوم لازم لعلته المعينة، لا يمكن تخلف المعلول عن علته التامة التي دخل فيها وجود الشروط وانتفاء الموانع.
The first type: Indeed the distinction between first principles and others, that first principles are what have the subject's affirmation to the predicate, which is the affirmation of the attribute to the described, and the thing judged to the thing judged about, and the thing reported to the thing reported about, like the affirmation of the predicate to the subject, by distinguishing between the 'primary' and other, that if the subject is affirmed to the predicate by itself in both existences—mental and external—then it is primary, and if it depends on a middle term, then it is not primary, is a corrupt distinction based on a corrupt foundation: that among the necessary attributes of the described, some are necessary by themselves without any middle term between them and the described in reality, and some are not necessary by themselves but by a middle term in reality, that middle term being necessary for the described and this predicate being necessary for that middle term. This distinction has been mentioned by more than one, like al-Razi and others regarding necessary attributes. Ibn Sina also mentioned it, but Ibn Sina said that by 'middle term' he meant 'the middle term in the syllogism', which is what is associated with the lam in saying 'because'. And this is the proof, and the proof is a middle term in the mind for the reasoner, not a middle term in the very affirmation of the attribute to the described, for one may infer the effect from the cause, as one infers the cause from the effect, and one infers one of two effects from the other, and infers the existence of one of two opposites from the non-existence of the other, and infers the existence of one of two concomitants from the realization of the other. There is no doubt that the necessary attributes of the described divide into what is self-evident in its necessity to a human, and what is not self-evident but its necessity requires a proof. And its being self-evident or not self-evident to a human is not the thing in itself, but rather it is a report about the human's knowledge of it and a reminder. So it is a report about mental existence, not external. So what was self-evident to a human, known to him, existing in his mind, he did not need a proof for it. And what was not such, he needed a proof for it. And a thing's being self-evident or not is a relation and an addition between the known and the knowing human. And people's states differ in this: it may become clear to Zayd what does not become clear to Amr. For the causes of knowledge, the strength of perception, and the quality of minds are varied. So it does not follow that if the affirmation of some attributes or their necessity or the description of the described with them becomes clear to a human, that it becomes clear to everyone; nor does it follow that if it is hidden from some people, it is hidden from everyone. So then, if one distinguishes between the primary and other by saying the primary does not need a middle term, then the proposition's being primary or non-primary is an additional distinction depending on people's states. So that would be comparable to saying: the proposition is either known or not known, or apparent or not apparent, or clear or not clear, or evident or not evident, or a human imagines its truth or does not imagine it. And this is a correct distinction, for every proposition in relation to every person is either self-evident to him or not self-evident to him. But this distinction does not distinguish between genres of propositions such that one genre entirely belongs to the non-self-evident and another genre entirely belongs to the self-evident. For this distinction does not revert to a necessary attribute of the proposition, as they claimed: that the self-evident necessary is what is affirmed to the described without a middle term in reality, and the non-self-evident necessary is what its affirmation is by a middle term in reality. Rather, all necessary attributes of the described have no middle term between them and the described at all in reality. And if a human needs a proof in his knowledge of their affirmation, not everything that is not known to be necessary for the described except by a proof has its affirmation only by a middle term, as its explanation preceded. For the effect is necessary for its specific cause; it is impossible for the effect to lag behind its complete cause, which includes the existence of conditions and the absence of impediments.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the logicians' distinction between first principles (awwaliyat) and common notions (mashhurat). He begins by stating the logicians' definition: first principles are those in which the subject is affirmed to the predicate by itself in both mental and external existence, without needing a middle term; otherwise it is not a first principle. Ibn Taymiyya declares this distinction corrupt, built on a corrupt foundation. The foundation is the claim that among the necessary attributes of a subject, some are self-evident without any middle term in reality, while others require a middle term in reality. He notes that this distinction was made by al-Razi and others, and also by Ibn Sina, but Ibn Sina clarified that by 'middle term' he meant the middle term in a syllogism, i.e., the proof (dalil). Ibn Sina's point is that the proof is a middle term in the mind of the reasoner, not a middle term in the actual ontological connection between attribute and subject. Ibn Taymiyya agrees with this epistemic interpretation and uses it to attack the notion that necessity can be ontologically divided into 'with' and 'without' a middle term. He then argues that all necessary attributes have no middle term in reality between them and their subject; the necessity is direct. The distinction between self-evident and non-self-evident is merely epistemological: it depends on the human knower. What is self-evident to one person may require proof for another, due to differences in knowledge, perception, and mental capacity. Therefore, the logicians' distinction is not a division of propositions into fixed genera (jins) but a relative distinction based on individual knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the distinction cannot be used to classify propositions as inherently self-evident or non-self-evident; it is merely a contextual judgment. He reinforces this by stating that effect is necessarily tied to its complete cause; there is no ontological gap. Thus, the logicians' claim that some necessary attributes require a middle term in reality is false.
