المقام الرابع - الوجه الحادي عشر : اليوم الآخر كما هو مذكور في القرآن، إنما تعاد النفوسُ العالمة دون الجاهلة فإن العالمة تبقى بالعلم فإن النفس تبقى ببقاء معلومها والجاهلة التي ليس لها معلوم باقٍ تَفْسُد وهذا قول طائفة من أعيانهم، ولهم فيه مصنفات. ومنهم من ينكر معادَ الأنفس كما يُنكر معاد الأبدان. وهو قول طوائف منهم. وكثير منهم يقول بالتناسخ. وليس شيء من ذلك إيماناً باليوم الآخر. فإن اليوم الآخِرَ هو الذي ذكره الله في قوله تعالى : ﴿رَبَّنَا إِنَّكَ جَامِعُ النَّاسِ لِيَوْمٍ لا رَيْبَ فِيهِ﴾ [سورة آل عمران : ٩]. وقوله تعالى : ﴿قُلْ إِنَّ الْأَوَّلِينَ وَالْآخِرِينَ لَمَجْمُوعُونَ إِلَى مِيقَاتِ يَوْمٍ مَعْلُومٍ﴾ [سورة الواقعة : ٥٠/٤٩]. وقوله تعالى : ﴿زَعَمَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَنْ لَنْ يُبْعَثُوا قُلْ بَلَى وَرَبِّي لَتُبْعَثُنَّ ثُمَّ لَتُنَبَّؤُنَّ بِمَا عَمِلْتُمْ وَذَلِكَ عَلَى اللَّهِ يَسِيرٌ﴾ إلى قوله : ﴿يَوْمَ يَجْمَعُكُمْ لِيَوْمِ الْجَمْعِ ذَلِكَ يَوْمُ التَّغَابُنِ﴾ [سورة التغابن : ٧-٩]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا الرُّسُلُ أُقِّتَتْ لِأَيِّ يَوْمٍ أُجِّلَتْ لِيَوْمِ الْفَصْلِ﴾ [سورة المرسلات : ١١-١٥]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَةً لِمَنْ خَافَ عَذَابَ الْآخِرَةِ ذَلِكَ يَوْمٌ مَجْمُوعٌ لَهُ النَّاسُ وَذَلِكَ يَوْمٌ مَشْهُودٌ﴾ [سورة هود : ١٠٣-١٠٥]. وقوله: ﴿وَيْلٌ لِلْمُطَفِّفِينَ الَّذِينَ إِذَا اكْتَالُوا عَلَى النَّاسِ يَسْتَوْفُونَ﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿يَوْمَ يَقُومُ النَّاسُ لِرَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ﴾ [سورة المطففين : ١-٦]. وفي الصحيح عن النبي ﷺ أنه قال: «يوم يقوم الناس لرب العالمين - يقوم أحدهم في العرق إلى أنصاف أُذنيه». وقوله: ﴿الْقَارِعَةُ مَا الْقَارِعَةُ﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿يَوْمَ يَكُونُ النَّاسُ كَالْفَرَاشِ الْمَبْثُوثِ﴾ [سورة القارعة : ١-٥]. وقوله: ﴿فَإِذَا نُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ نَفْخَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ وَحُمِلَتِ الْأَرْضُ وَالْجِبَالُ فَدُكَّتَا دَكَّةً وَاحِدَةً﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿يَوْمَئِذٍ تُعْرَضُونَ لا تَخْفَى مِنْكُمْ خَافِيَةٌ﴾ [سورة الحاقة : ١٣-١٨]. وقوله: ﴿وَيَقُولُونَ أَئِذَا مِتْنَا وَكُنَّا تُرَابًا وَعِظَامًا أَئِنَّا لَمَبْعُوثُونَ﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿إِنَّهُمْ مَسْئُولُونَ﴾ [سورة الصافات : ١٦-٢٦]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿سَأَلَ سَائِلٌ بِعَذَابٍ وَاقِعٍ لِلْكَافِرِينَ لَيْسَ لَهُ دَافِعٌ﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿يَوَدُّ الْمُجْرِمُ لَوْ يَفْتَدِي مِنْ عَذَابِ يَوْمِئِذٍ بِبَنِيهِ﴾ [سورة المعارج : ١-١١]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَذَرْهُمْ يَخُوضُوا وَيَلْعَبُوا حَتَّى يُلَاقُوا يَوْمَهُمُ الَّذِي يُوعَدُونَ يَوْمَ يَخْرُجُونَ مِنَ الْأَجْدَاثِ سِرَاعًا﴾ [سورة المعارج : ٤٢-٤٤]. وقوله: ﴿فَتَوَلَّ عَنْهُمْ يَوْمَ يَدْعُ الدَّاعِ إِلَى شَيْءٍ نُكُرٍ خُشَّعًا أَبْصَارُهُمْ يَخْرُجُونَ مِنَ الْأَجْدَاثِ كَأَنَّهُمْ جَرَادٌ مُنْتَشِرٌ﴾ [سورة القمر : ٦-٨]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَكَيْفَ تَتَّقُونَ إِنْ كَفَرْتُمْ يَوْمًا يَجْعَلُ الْوِلْدَانَ شِيبًا السَّمَاءُ مُنْفَطِرٌ بِهِ﴾ [سورة المزمل : ١٧-١٨]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ زَلْزَلَةَ السَّاعَةِ شَيْءٌ عَظِيمٌ يَوْمَ تَرَوْنَهَا تَذْهَلُ كُلُّ مُرْضِعَةٍ عَمَّا أَرْضَعَتْ﴾ [سورة الحج : ١-٢]. ومثل هذا في القرآن كثير. فهؤلاء لا يؤمنون باليوم الآخر. فلم يدخلوا في من مدح من الصابئين.
The Fourth Station - The Eleventh Aspect: The Last Day as mentioned in the Qur'an. Souls of the knowledgeable are resurrected, not the ignorant; for the knowledgeable soul persists through knowledge, since the soul persists by the persistence of its object of knowledge, while the ignorant soul, having no persisting object of knowledge, perishes. This is the saying of a group of their leading figures, and they have authored works on it. Some of them deny the resurrection of souls just as they deny the resurrection of bodies, and this is the saying of groups among them. Many of them hold reincarnation. None of that constitutes belief in the Last Day. For the Last Day is what God mentioned in His words: 'Our Lord, indeed You will gather the people for a Day about which there is no doubt' [Surah Al-Imran: 9]; and His words: 'Say, indeed the former and latter will be gathered to the appointment of a known Day' [Surah Al-Waqi'ah: 49-50]; and His words: 'Those who disbelieve claim that they will never be resurrected. Say, Yes, by my Lord, you will surely be resurrected; then you will surely be informed of what you did, and that is easy for God' up to His words: 'The Day He will gather you for the Day of Assembly; that is the Day of Mutual Disappointment' [Surah At-Taghabun: 7-9]; and His words: 'And when the messengers are appointed for which Day they are appointed? For the Day of Decision' [Surah Al-Mursalat: 11-15]; and His words: 'Indeed in that is a sign for whoever fears the punishment of the Hereafter. That is a Day for which the people will be gathered, and that is a witnessed Day' [Surah Hud: 103-105]; and His words: 'Woe to the defrauders...' up to 'The Day when mankind will stand before the Lord of the worlds' [Surah Al-Mutaffifin: 1-6]; and in the Sahih from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'On the Day when mankind stands before the Lord of the worlds, one of them will be submerged in sweat up to the middle of his ears.' And His words: 'The Striking Calamity, what is the Striking Calamity? ... on the Day when people will be like scattered moths' [Surah Al-Qari'ah: 1-5]; and His words: 'And when the Trumpet is blown with one blast, and the earth and the mountains are lifted and crushed with one crushing... on that Day you will be presented, none of your secrets will be hidden' [Surah Al-Haqqah: 13-18]; and His words: 'And they say, When we have died and become dust and bones, are we indeed to be resurrected? ... Indeed they are accountable' [Surah As-Saffat: 16-26]; and His words: 'A questioner asked about a punishment bound to happen for the disbelievers, which none can avert... the criminal wishes he could ransom himself from the punishment of that Day by his children' [Surah Al-Ma'arij: 1-11]; and His words: 'So leave them to indulge in vain talk and play until they meet their Day which they are promised - the Day they will come out of the graves swiftly' [Surah Al-Ma'arij: 42-44]; and His words: 'So turn away from them on the Day when the caller calls to something terrible. With eyes humbled, they will come out of the graves as if they were scattered locusts' [Surah Al-Qamar: 6-8]; and His words: 'Then how can you avoid punishment, if you disbelieve, on a Day that will make the children gray-headed? The heaven will split open thereby; His promise is to be fulfilled' [Surah Al-Muzzammil: 17-18]; and His words: 'Indeed the convulsion of the Hour is a terrible thing. On the Day you see it, every nursing mother will forget what she nursed...' [Surah Al-Hajj: 1-2]. And much of this is in the Qur'an. So these people do not believe in the Last Day. Thus they are not included among those praised from the Sabians.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the philosophers' doctrine regarding the afterlife. The author, Ibn Taymiyya, begins by presenting the philosophical view that only the souls of the knowledgeable are resurrected, because they persist through their knowledge, while ignorant souls perish. He mentions that some philosophers deny the resurrection of souls and bodies entirely, while others believe in reincarnation (tanasukh). Ibn Taymiyya then asserts that none of these beliefs constitute true faith in the Last Day as described in the Qur'an. He proceeds to cite numerous Qur'anic verses that depict the Last Day as a day of bodily resurrection, judgment, and accountability, involving all people—both the first and the last—gathered before God. These verses describe physical events such as the blowing of the trumpet, the earth being crushed, people emerging from graves, and the overwhelming nature of that Day. The author emphasizes that the philosophers' limited or metaphorical understanding of resurrection contradicts the clear Qur'anic text. He concludes that such individuals do not truly believe in the Last Day and are therefore not among those praised from the Sabians (or any people of faith). This passage exemplifies Ibn Taymiyya's method of critiquing Greek-influenced philosophical ideas by contrasting them with explicit scriptural evidence.

Key Terms
اليوم الآخر
المعاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following physical details is NOT mentioned in the Qur'anic verses cited by Ibn Taymiyya in this passage?
A) People emerging from graves swiftly.
B) The earth and mountains being crushed.
C) People being resurrected with wings.
D) Nursing mothers forgetting their infants.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an describes the Last Day with vivid physical details that establish it as a real, bodily event, incompatible with philosophical reinterpretations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refutation of Philosophers' Conception of Human Perfection
Author critiques philosophers' intellectualist perfection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' reduction of human perfection to intellectual knowledge, and contrast it with the prophetic conception.

Core Idea
Philosophers reduce human perfection to knowledge; prophets perfect the soul through love and worship.

Ibn Taymiyya here targets the core of the philosophers' ethical and spiritual project. They claim that the ultimate goal is refinement of the soul to acquire knowledge, especially knowledge of absolute existence, making man an intellectual world parallel to the cosmos. Ibn Taymiyya counters that this falls short of what the prophets brought, which involves both knowledge and practice—love of Allah and worship. He exposes the philosophical errors: ignoring the practical power of the soul, limiting perfection to universal concepts rather than specific existents, and ultimately seeking assimilation to the celestial sphere rather than worship of the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim
Locate where Ibn Taymiyya states what the philosophers say about the perfection of the soul (kamāl al-nafs). They claim it is achieved through intellectual knowledge, specifically knowledge of 'absolute existence' (al-wujūd al-muṭlaq) or the Necessary Existent, so that man becomes an intellectual world parallel to the existing world.
This claim is found in the lines beginning with 'وهؤلاء جعلوا كمالها في العلم فقط' and further.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's grounds of critique
Determine the type of objection Ibn Taymiyya raises. He uses both epistemological and revelation-based grounds: (1) The prophets teach that perfection is through love and worship, not mere knowledge; (2) The philosophers' metaphysics is mostly ignorance; (3) They erroneously think perfection is attained through universal concepts rather than specific existents.
Ibn Taymiyya explicitly lists these errors: 'غلطوا من وجوه منها ظنّهم أن كمال النفس في مجرد العلم...'.
3
Unpack each stated error
Explain each error: (a) Limiting perfection to the cognitive power ignores the practical power (love, worship). (b) Seeking universal knowledge rather than knowledge of specific created beings leads to abstraction. (c) Their claim to have knowledge in metaphysics is false; most of it is ignorance.
These errors undermine the philosophers' entire ethical framework.
4
Identify the ultimate goal of the philosophers
Ibn Taymiyya states that the philosophers' ultimate goal is 'assimilation to the celestial sphere' (al-tashabbuh bil-falak). This reduces worship to bodily discipline and denies that Allah knows particulars or responds to supplication.
This goal is contrasted with the prophetic goal of worship and devotion.
5
Evaluate the critique
Assess whether Ibn Taymiyya's argument holds. Consider whether he fairly represents the philosophers' views and whether his own alternative (love and worship as perfection) is supported by revelation and reason.
This step encourages critical thinking about the strengths and limitations of the critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان بعض ضلالاتٍ مِنْ معتقدات الفلاسفة
وأيضاً فالأنبياء وأتباعهم بل وجماهير الأمم متفقون على أن الله خلق السموات والأرض. فهي محدثة بعد أن لم تكن وكذلك أساطين الفلاسفة والقول بقدمها هو كون العالم قديم عن أرسطو وشيعته ومن وافقهم. فكيف يجوز أن يقال: إن الحكمة التي أمر الله نبيه أن يدعو الخلق بها هو هذا؟ وأيضاً فحكمتهم غايتها تعديل أخلاق النفس لتستعد للعلم الذي هو كمالها. وهذا لا تكمل من أقل ما جاءت به الرسل ومن توابعه والمقصود بالعبادات التي أَمَرَت بها الرسلُ تكميل النفس بمحبة الله تعالى وتألّهه. فإن النفس لها قوتان - علمية وعملية. وهؤلاء جعلوا كمالها [٤٦٢] في العلم فقط ، ثم ظنُّوا ذلك هو العلم بالوجود المطلق حتى يصير الإنسان عالماً معقولاً موازياً للعالم الموجود ومنهم من يقول : النفس إنما تبقى ببقاء معلومها، وهم يعتقدون بقاء الأفلاك، والعقول، والنفوس . فجعلوا كمالها في العلم /٤٦١ بالموجودات التي اعتقدوا بقاءَها. ومن تقرب إلى الإسلام منهم يقول : بل كمالها في العلم بواجب الوجود وهذا يشبه قول الجهم بن صفوان ومن وافقه في أن «الإيمان مجرَّدُ العلم بالله . وقد بسطنا الكلام على هذا في غير هذا الموضع في جواب «المسئلة الصفدية» وغير ذلك، وبينا أنهم غلطوا من وجوه منها ظنّهم أن كمال النفس في مجرد العلم ؛ ومنها ظنهم أن هذا الكمال يحصل بمعرفة أمور كلية لا موجودات معينة؛ ومنها ظنهم أن ما عندهم في الإلهيات علم، وأكثره جهل. ولهذا كان الغاية عندهم التشبه بالفلك . ولهذا يصنف من يصنف منهم في الصلاة فليس المقصود منها عبادة الله ولا مقصود الصلاة دعاؤه، فإنه لا يعلم الجزئيات عندهم ولا يميّز بين المصلي وغير المصلي. بل مقصود الصلاة هو العلم بالوجود المطلق الذي يزعمون أنه كمال النفس. والصلاة الظاهرة يُطلب منها سياسة البدن ورياضته. وإنما قالوا إن فإذن حقيقة الصلوة علم الله سبحانه وتعالى بوحدانيته ووجوب وجوده وتنزيه ذاته وتقديس صفاته في سوانح الإخلاص في صلاته - ص ۸. فاعلم أن الصلاة منقسمة قسمين ـ قسم منها ظاهر =
Explanation of some misguidance from the beliefs of the philosophers. And also, the prophets and their followers, indeed the majority of nations, agree that Allah created the heavens and the earth. They are originated after not having been. Likewise, the pillars of philosophy and the statement that the world is eternal is the view of Aristotle and his sect and those who agree with them. So how can it be said that the wisdom with which Allah commanded His Prophet to call the creation is this? And also, their wisdom, its goal is the refinement of the soul's morals to prepare it for knowledge, which is its perfection. But this is not perfected by the least of what the prophets brought and its concomitants. And the purpose of the acts of worship that the prophets commanded is the perfection of the soul through love of Allah Almighty and devotion to Him. For the soul has two powers: cognitive and practical. These people made its perfection only in knowledge, then they thought that this is knowledge of absolute existence, so that man becomes an intellectual world parallel to the existing world. And among them are those who say: the soul only persists by the persistence of its object of knowledge, and they believe in the persistence of the spheres, intellects, and souls. So they made its perfection in knowledge of the existents which they believed persist. And whoever among them draws near to Islam says: rather its perfection is in knowledge of the Necessary Existent, and this resembles the saying of Jahm ibn Safwan and those who agreed with him that 'faith is merely knowledge of Allah.' We have expanded the discussion on this in other places, in the response to 'al-Mas'alah al-Safadiyyah' and elsewhere, and we have shown that they erred in several ways: among them their assumption that the perfection of the soul is in mere knowledge; among them their assumption that this perfection is attained by knowing universal matters rather than specific existents; among them their assumption that what they have in metaphysics is knowledge, while most of it is ignorance. Hence their ultimate goal is assimilation to the celestial sphere. Hence whoever among them writes about prayer, the purpose of it is not worship of Allah, nor is the purpose of prayer supplication to Him, because according to them He does not know particulars and does not distinguish between the one praying and the one not praying. Rather, the purpose of prayer is knowledge of absolute existence, which they claim is the perfection of the soul. And the outward prayer is sought for the management and discipline of the body. They only said that the reality of prayer is knowledge of Allah Almighty of His oneness, necessary existence, transcendence of His essence, and sanctification of His attributes in the moments of sincerity in his prayer. Know that prayer is divided into two parts: an outward part and...
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the philosophers' beliefs, likely by Ibn Taymiyya. He begins by stating that prophets and the majority of nations agree that the world is created, while the philosophers (especially Aristotle and his followers) claim it is eternal. He questions how the wisdom that Allah commanded His Prophet to call to could be this philosophy. Then he attacks the philosophers' goal: they aim to refine the soul's morals to attain knowledge as its perfection. Ibn Taymiyya argues that this is far less than what the prophets brought; the prophets' purpose is the perfection of the soul through love of Allah and devotion. The soul has two powers: cognitive and practical. The philosophers restrict perfection to the cognitive, specifically knowledge of 'absolute existence' such that man becomes an intellectual world parallel to the existing world. Some philosophers say the soul persists through its object of knowledge, believing in the persistence of celestial spheres, intellects, and souls. Those influenced by Islam among them say perfection is knowledge of the Necessary Existent, which resembles the Jahmi position that faith is mere knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya then notes he has explained their errors elsewhere: they think perfection is in mere knowledge, that it is attained through universal concepts rather than specific existents, and that their metaphysical claims are mostly ignorance. Their ultimate goal is assimilation to the celestial sphere. Consequently, their writings on prayer miss the point: prayer is not for worship or supplication (since they deny Allah knows particulars), but for knowledge of absolute existence. The outward prayer is merely bodily discipline. He quotes Ibn Sina's view that the reality of prayer is knowledge of Allah's oneness, necessary existence, etc. This shows the philosophers reduce worship to intellectual exercise.

Key Terms
كمال النفس
الوجود المطلق
التشبه بالفلك

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) They limit perfection to intellectual knowledge and ignore the practical and devotional aspects.
C) They believe the soul is mortal.
D) They deny the existence of the soul.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' intellectualist conception of human perfection is deficient because it ignores the practical power of the soul and the prophetic emphasis on love and worship.

The Soul's Perfection: Mere Knowledge or Love of God?
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the philosophers' definition of soul's perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the philosophers' doctrine of soul's perfection as mere knowledge and contrast it with Ibn Taymiyya's insistence on both cognitive and practical powers culminating in love of God.

Core Idea
Philosophers reduce the soul to intellect; Ibn Taymiyya restores its heart.

Ibn Taymiyya attacks the foundational assumption of the falasifa that the soul's perfection (kamal al-nafs) is purely cognitive. He insists the soul has two powers—cognitive and practical—and true perfection involves both, culminating in love of God and devoted worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim about soul's perfection
Locate the statement that the philosophers make the soul's perfection solely in knowledge ('ilm). They say: 'كمالها في العلم فقط'.
This is the target of Ibn Taymiyya's critique.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's analysis of the soul
Find where he says the soul has two powers (quwwatan): cognitive ('ilmiyya) and practical ('amaliyya).
This is the key analytical distinction.
3
Contrast the two models of perfection
The philosophers perfect only the cognitive power; Ibn Taymiyya insists both must be perfected. The practical power is perfected through love and devotion.
4
Recognize the link to Jahm's reduction of faith
Ibn Taymiyya compares the philosophers' view to Jahm bin Safwan, who said faith is mere knowledge of God.
This shows the theological danger of reducing worship to intellect.

Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the philosophers' (falasifa) understanding of the purpose of prayer and the perfection of the soul. He begins by setting the context: the philosophers' claim that the world is pre-eternal (qadim) like their master Aristotle and his followers. He then asks how the wisdom (hikma) that God commanded His Prophet to call to could be this. He states that their wisdom aims to adjust the soul's morals to prepare it for knowledge, which they consider its perfection. However, this does not even complete the least of what the prophets brought. The true purpose of worship commanded by the prophets is to perfect the soul through love of God and devotion to Him (tahalluh). Ibn Taymiyya notes that the soul has two powers: cognitive (ilmiyya) and practical (amaliyya). The philosophers restrict perfection to the cognitive alone, and they imagine that this knowledge is knowledge of absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq), such that a person becomes a pure intellect parallel to the existing world. Some of them say the soul subsists by the subsistence of its known objects, and they believe in the subsistence of the celestial spheres, intellects, and souls, so they place perfection in knowledge of those enduring existents. Among those who try to align with Islam (al-mutaqarribun ila al-Islam), some say perfection is in knowledge of the Necessary Existent (Wajib al-Wujud), resembling the Jahmiyya who define faith as mere knowledge of God. Ibn Taymiyya states he has elaborated elsewhere (in his answer to the Safadian question) on their errors: (1) assuming perfection is merely in knowledge, (2) assuming it is attained through universal concepts rather than specific existents, and (3) assuming their theology is knowledge when most is ignorance. Consequently, their ultimate goal becomes assimilation to the celestial sphere (tashabbuh bi-l-falak). Hence, when they write about prayer, they do not intend worship of God or supplication to Him, because according to them God does not know particulars and does not distinguish between the one praying and the one not praying. Rather, their intended purpose of prayer is knowledge of absolute existence, which they claim is the soul's perfection. The outward prayer is merely for the discipline and training of the body. They claim the reality of prayer is knowledge of God's oneness, necessity, transcendence, etc., as quoted from Ibn Sina. Ibn Taymiyya then critiques their view of supplication: according to them, God does not hear servants nor see their actions nor answer prayers. Instead, supplication is the soul's manipulation of the world's matter (hayula) through detachment from the body. The Lord (al-Rabb) for them is not all-knowing or all-powerful; rather, the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al) is the one that manages the world and is asked from. They do not affirm angels descending and ascending, nor that good speech or righteous deeds ascend to God. The ultimate goal for souls is to connect with the active intellect, not to ascend to God. When they speak of the vision of God (ru'yat Allah), they interpret it as knowledge of absolute existence or of the Necessary Existent. Ibn Taymiyya then references the author of 'the books withheld from those not worthy of them' (likely al-Ghazali) discussing the vision of the Truth in al-Ihya or elsewhere, implying that even al-Ghazali's esoteric interpretations align with the philosophers.

Key Terms
كمال النفس
القوتان العلمية والعملية
محبة الله
التألّه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what do the philosophers (falasifa) believe is the perfection of the soul?
A) Love of God and devotion
B) Knowledge of absolute existence or the Necessary Existent
C) Assimilation to the celestial sphere
D) Discipline of the body and morals

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya reveals that the philosophers' purely intellectual perfection of the soul contradicts the prophetic purpose of worship, which integrates knowledge with love and devotion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a debate with a philosopher who claims that the goal of worship is to acquire knowledge of God, write a response using Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the soul has two powers and perfection requires both love and action.
?
Identify a contemporary reduction of worship to mere intellectual study (e.g., focusing only on 'ilm without 'amal) and explain, using Ibn Taymiyya's critique, why this is incomplete.

The Philosophers' Purpose of Prayer: Knowledge, Not Worship
Ibn Taymiyya critiques the philosophers' reduction of prayer to an intellectual exercise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the philosophers' reinterpretation of prayer as a means to attain knowledge of absolute existence and contrast it with the Islamic view of prayer as worship and supplication to God.

Core Idea
Philosophers turn prayer into intellectual exercise; Islam makes it a direct connection to Allah.

Having critiqued the philosophers' concept of soul's perfection, Ibn Taymiyya now attacks their view of prayer. He shows that, according to them, prayer is not about worshipping God or supplication—since God does not know particulars—but rather about attaining knowledge of absolute existence and assimilating to the celestial sphere.

Guided Path
1
Find the philosophers' claimed purpose of prayer
Look for the statement that the purpose of prayer (salat) is knowledge of absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq), not worship of God.
Ibn Taymiyya quotes them saying: 'مقصود الصلاة هو العلم بالوجود المطلق'.
2
Identify the consequence of their theology
According to philosophers, God does not know particulars, so He cannot hear prayers or distinguish worshippers. Hence supplication is pointless.
This is a direct implication of their metaphysical system.
3
Note the role of outward prayer
Outward prayer (al-salat al-zahira) is only for disciplining the body, not for connecting with God.
It is reduced to a mere physical exercise.
4
Understand the ultimate goal: assimilation to the sphere
The philosophers' end goal (al-ghaya) is tashabbuh bi-l-falak (assimilation to the celestial sphere), which means aligning the soul with the cosmic order, not with God.
This contrasts sharply with the Islamic goal of seeking nearness to Allah.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الحادي عشر : المقصود هو تذكر الشرع حادثاً غير والأرض. فهي محدثة بعد أن لم تكن وكذلك أساطين الفلاسفة والقول بقدمها هو كون العالم عن أرسطو وشيعته ومن وافقهم. فكيف يجوز أن يقال: إن الحكمة التي أمر الله نبيه أن يدعو الخلق بها هو هذا؟ قديم النفس بمجرد العلم وأيضاً فحكمتهم غايتها تعديل أخلاق النفس لتستعد للعلم الذي هو كمالها. وهذا لا تكمل من أقل ما جاءت به الرسل ومن توابعه والمقصود بالعبادات التي أَمَرَت بها الرسلُ تكميل النفس بمحبة الله تعالى وتألّهه. فإن النفس لها قوتان - علمية وعملية. وهؤلاء جعلوا كمالها في العلم فقط ، ثم ظنُّوا ذلك هو العلم بالوجود المطلق حتى يصير الإنسان عالماً معقولا موازياً للعالم الموجود ومنهم من يقول : النفس إنما تبقى ببقاء معلومها، وهم يعتقدون بقاء الأفلاك، والعقول، والنفوس . فجعلوا كمالها في العلم بالموجودات التي اعتقدوا بقاءَها. ومن تقرب إلى الإسلام منهم يقول : بل كمالها في العلم بواجب الوجود وهذا يشبه قول الجهم بن صفوان ومن وافقه في أن «الإيمان مجرَّدُ العلم بالله . وقد بسطنا الكلام على هذا في غير هذا الموضع في جواب «المسئلة الصفدية» وغير ذلك، وبينا أنهم غلطوا من وجوه منها ظنّهم أن كمال النفس في مجرد العلم ؛ ومنها ظنهم أن هذا الكمال يحصل بمعرفة أمور كلية لا موجودات معينة؛ ومنها ظنهم أن ما عندهم في الإلهيات علم، وأكثره جهل. ولهذا كان الغاية عندهم التشبه بالفلك . ولهذا يصنف من يصنف منهم في الصلاة فليس المقصود منها عبادة الله ولا مقصود الصلاة دعاؤه، فإنه لا يعلم الجزئيات عندهم ولا يميّز بين المصلي وغير المصلي. بل مقصود الصلاة هو العلم بالوجود المطلق الذي يزعمون أنه كمال النفس. والصلاة الظاهرة يُطلب منها سياسة البدن ورياضته. وإنما قالوا إن حقيقة الصلوة علم الله سبحانه وتعالى بوحدانيته ووجوب وجوده وتنزيه ذاته وتقديس صفاته في سوانح الإخلاص في صلاته - ص ۸. فاعلم أن الصلاة منقسمة قسمين ـ قسم منها ظاهر = المقصود هو كتاب الرد على المنطقيين يسأل القمر ويستعيده فإنه يدبّر هذا العالم بواسطة العقل الفعال. فهو عندهم الرب الذي يُسأل ويُستعاذ به، ومنه فاضت العلوم على الأنبياء وغيرهم. وربما قالوا : المقصود بالصلاة تذكُرُ الشرع الذي شرَعَه الشارع ليُحفظ به القانون تذكر الشرع الذي شرعه لهم لمصلحة الدنيا ، كما يذكر ذلك ابن سينا وغيره . وذلك أنهم لا يثبتون الحق عندهم من أن الله يسمع كلام العباد ولا يَرَى أفعالهم ولا يُجيب دعاءهم. بل الدعاء عندهم هو تصرف النفس في هَيُولى العالم فيحصل لها بما تهتم به من تجردها عن البدن نوع تجريد حتى تتصرف في هيولى العالم. وأما الرب تعالى فليس هو عندهم لا بكل شيء عليم، ولا على كل شيء قدير، ولا يعلم لا السرّ ولا النجوى ولا غير ذلك أحوال العباد، ولا له ملائكة كثيرون ينزلون ويَصْعَدون إليه عندهم، ولا يَصْعَدُ إليه لا الكلم الطيب ولا العمل الصالح وغاية الأنفس عندهم أن تكون متصلة بالعقل الفعال الذي هو ربُّها عندهم، لا تَصْعَدُ إلى الله . المراد برؤية وإذا قالوا سعادة النفس أن تشهد الله وأن تراه فحقيقة ذلك عندهم هو العلم بما تصوَّرَتُه من الوجود المطلق أو من وجود واجب الوجود. وصاحب «الكُتُب المضنون بها على غير أهلها» إذا تكلم في رؤية الحق ورؤية وجهه في كتابه «الأحياء» أو غيره
The fourth station - the eleventh aspect: The purpose is to remember the Sharia as originated and not. And the earth. So they are originated after not being, and likewise the pillars of the philosophers, and the statement of their pre-existence is the world being from Aristotle and his sect and those who agreed with them. So how can it be said that the wisdom which God commanded His Prophet to call the creation to is this? The soul is pre-existent by mere knowledge. Also, their wisdom's goal is to adjust the soul's morals to prepare it for knowledge, which is its perfection. And this does not complete the least of what the Messengers brought and its followers. And the purpose of the acts of worship which the Messengers commanded is to perfect the soul with love of God Almighty and devotedness to Him. Indeed, the soul has two powers - cognitive and practical. And these people made its perfection only in knowledge, then they thought that is knowledge of absolute existence until man becomes an intellect in potentiality parallel to the existing world. And among them are those who say: The soul only remains by the subsistence of its known object, and they believe in the subsistence of the spheres, intellects, and souls. So they made its perfection in knowledge of the existents whose subsistence they believed. And whoever approaches Islam among them says: Rather, its perfection is in knowledge of the Necessary Existent, and this resembles the saying of Jahm bin Safwan and those who agreed with him that 'faith is mere knowledge of God.' And we have expanded the speech on this in other places in the answer to 'the Safadian question' and elsewhere, and we explained that they erred in respects, including their assumption that the perfection of the soul is in mere knowledge; and their assumption that this perfection is obtained by knowledge of universal matters, not specific existents; and their assumption that what they have in theology is knowledge, while most of it is ignorance. Hence, the goal for them was assimilation to the sphere. Hence, whoever among them classifies concerning prayer, the purpose of it is not worship of God, nor is the purpose of prayer supplication to Him, since He does not know particulars according to them, nor does He distinguish between the one praying and the one not praying. Rather, the purpose of prayer is knowledge of absolute existence, which they claim is the perfection of the soul. And the outward prayer is sought for the governance and discipline of the body. And they said that the reality of prayer is knowledge of God Almighty of His oneness, necessity of existence, transcendence of His essence, and sanctification of His attributes in the flashes of sincerity in his prayer - p. 8. So know that prayer is divided into two parts - a part that is outward = The purpose is The Book of Refutation of the Logicians: He asks the moon and seeks refuge from it, for it manages this world through the active intellect. So it is according to them the lord who is asked and sought refuge from, and from it sciences overflow to the prophets and others. And perhaps they said: The purpose of prayer is to remember the Sharia which the Lawgiver legislated to preserve the law, remembering the Sharia which He legislated for them for the benefit of the world, as Ibn Sina and others mention. That is because they do not affirm according to them the truth that God hears the speech of servants, nor sees their actions, nor answers their supplication. Rather, supplication according to them is the soul's manipulation in the matter of the world, so it obtains by what it cares about from its detachment from the body a type of detachment until it manipulates the matter of the world. As for the Lord Almighty, He is not according to them knowing of all things, nor powerful over all things, nor does He know secret or whispered discourse or other than that of the states of servants, nor does He have many angels descending and ascending to Him according to them, nor does good speech or righteous deed ascend to Him, and the utmost of souls according to them is to be connected to the active intellect, which is their lord, not to ascend to God. The intended meaning of vision: And when they say the happiness of the soul is to witness God and see Him, the reality of that according to them is knowledge of what they conceived of absolute existence or of the existence of the Necessary Existent. And the author of 'the books withheld from those not worthy of them' when he speaks about the vision of the Truth and the vision of His face in his book 'al-Ihya' or elsewhere.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the philosophers' (falasifa) understanding of the purpose of prayer and the perfection of the soul. Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, why do the philosophers deny that prayer involves supplication (du'a) to God?
A) Because they believe prayer is only for bodily discipline
B) Because they believe God does not know particulars and therefore cannot hear prayers
C) Because they think supplication is only for prophets

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
A philosopher argues that the purpose of prayer is to gain knowledge of God's attributes. Write a rebuttal using Ibn Taymiyya's point that such a view reduces prayer to an intellectual exercise and ignores its essence as worship and supplication.

Examine the statement 'Prayer is a conversation with Allah.' Explain how Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers shows why this statement is meaningful only if Allah knows particulars and responds.

The Active Intellect: The Philosophers' Substitute for God
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the philosophers' replacement of God with the active intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the philosophers' doctrine that the active intellect ('aql fa''al) is the true object of supplication and connection for souls, and contrast it with the Islamic belief that God alone is worthy of worship and supplication.

Core Idea
Philosophers replace Allah with the active intellect as the lord of souls.

Ibn Taymiyya reveals a shocking consequence of the philosophers' system: they effectively substitute the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al) for God. This intellect manages the sublunar world, answers prayers, and is the ultimate destination for human souls. In contrast, the God of Islam knows all, hears all, and is the only true object of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the active intellect's role in the philosophers' system
Find where Ibn Taymiyya says that the philosophers ask the moon and seek refuge from it, and that the active intellect manages this world and is the one asked and sought refuge from.
This is a direct quote from Ibn Sina or similar philosophers.
2
Note what God is denied
The philosophers deny that God knows particulars, hears servants, sees actions, or answers prayers. They also deny that angels ascend/descend and that good deeds ascend to Him.
This list shows the systematic replacement of divine attributes.
3
Understand the alternative account of supplication (du'a)
For the philosophers, supplication is not calling upon God; it is the soul's manipulation of the world's matter (hayula) through detachment from the body.
This is a naturalistic, almost magical, understanding.
4
Recognize the ultimate goal: connection with the active intellect
The utmost limit for souls is to connect with the active intellect, not to ascend to God.
This contrasts with the Islamic concept of meeting Allah and entering His mercy.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الحادي عشر : المقصود هو تذكر الشرع حادثاً غير والأرض. فهي محدثة بعد أن لم تكن وكذلك أساطين الفلاسفة والقول بقدمها هو كون العالم عن أرسطو وشيعته ومن وافقهم. فكيف يجوز أن يقال: إن الحكمة التي أمر الله نبيه أن يدعو الخلق بها هو هذا؟ قديم النفس بمجرد العلم وأيضاً فحكمتهم غايتها تعديل أخلاق النفس لتستعد للعلم الذي هو كمالها. وهذا لا تكمل من أقل ما جاءت به الرسل ومن توابعه والمقصود بالعبادات التي أَمَرَت بها الرسلُ تكميل النفس بمحبة الله تعالى وتألّهه. فإن النفس لها قوتان - علمية وعملية. وهؤلاء جعلوا كمالها في العلم فقط ، ثم ظنُّوا ذلك هو العلم بالوجود المطلق حتى يصير الإنسان عالماً معقولا موازياً للعالم الموجود ومنهم من يقول : النفس إنما تبقى ببقاء معلومها، وهم يعتقدون بقاء الأفلاك، والعقول، والنفوس . فجعلوا كمالها في العلم بالموجودات التي اعتقدوا بقاءَها. ومن تقرب إلى الإسلام منهم يقول : بل كمالها في العلم بواجب الوجود وهذا يشبه قول الجهم بن صفوان ومن وافقه في أن «الإيمان مجرَّدُ العلم بالله . وقد بسطنا الكلام على هذا في غير هذا الموضع في جواب «المسئلة الصفدية» وغير ذلك، وبينا أنهم غلطوا من وجوه منها ظنّهم أن كمال النفس في مجرد العلم ؛ ومنها ظنهم أن هذا الكمال يحصل بمعرفة أمور كلية لا موجودات معينة؛ ومنها ظنهم أن ما عندهم في الإلهيات علم، وأكثره جهل. ولهذا كان الغاية عندهم التشبه بالفلك . ولهذا يصنف من يصنف منهم في الصلاة فليس المقصود منها عبادة الله ولا مقصود الصلاة دعاؤه، فإنه لا يعلم الجزئيات عندهم ولا يميّز بين المصلي وغير المصلي. بل مقصود الصلاة هو العلم بالوجود المطلق الذي يزعمون أنه كمال النفس. والصلاة الظاهرة يُطلب منها سياسة البدن ورياضته. وإنما قالوا إن حقيقة الصلوة علم الله سبحانه وتعالى بوحدانيته ووجوب وجوده وتنزيه ذاته وتقديس صفاته في سوانح الإخلاص في صلاته - ص ۸. فاعلم أن الصلاة منقسمة قسمين ـ قسم منها ظاهر = المقصود هو كتاب الرد على المنطقيين يسأل القمر ويستعيده فإنه يدبّر هذا العالم بواسطة العقل الفعال. فهو عندهم الرب الذي يُسأل ويُستعاذ به، ومنه فاضت العلوم على الأنبياء وغيرهم. وربما قالوا : المقصود بالصلاة تذكُرُ الشرع الذي شرَعَه الشارع ليُحفظ به القانون تذكر الشرع الذي شرعه لهم لمصلحة الدنيا ، كما يذكر ذلك ابن سينا وغيره . وذلك أنهم لا يثبتون الحق عندهم من أن الله يسمع كلام العباد ولا يَرَى أفعالهم ولا يُجيب دعاءهم. بل الدعاء عندهم هو تصرف النفس في هَيُولى العالم فيحصل لها بما تهتم به من تجردها عن البدن نوع تجريد حتى تتصرف في هيولى العالم. وأما الرب تعالى فليس هو عندهم لا بكل شيء عليم، ولا على كل شيء قدير، ولا يعلم لا السرّ ولا النجوى ولا غير ذلك أحوال العباد، ولا له ملائكة كثيرون ينزلون ويَصْعَدون إليه عندهم، ولا يَصْعَدُ إليه لا الكلم الطيب ولا العمل الصالح وغاية الأنفس عندهم أن تكون متصلة بالعقل الفعال الذي هو ربُّها عندهم، لا تَصْعَدُ إلى الله . المراد برؤية وإذا قالوا سعادة النفس أن تشهد الله وأن تراه فحقيقة ذلك عندهم هو العلم بما تصوَّرَتُه من الوجود المطلق أو من وجود واجب الوجود. وصاحب «الكُتُب المضنون بها على غير أهلها» إذا تكلم في رؤية الحق ورؤية وجهه في كتابه «الأحياء» أو غيره
The fourth station - the eleventh aspect: The purpose is to remember the Sharia as originated and not. And the earth. So they are originated after not being, and likewise the pillars of the philosophers, and the statement of their pre-existence is the world being from Aristotle and his sect and those who agreed with them. So how can it be said that the wisdom which God commanded His Prophet to call the creation to is this? The soul is pre-existent by mere knowledge. Also, their wisdom's goal is to adjust the soul's morals to prepare it for knowledge, which is its perfection. And this does not complete the least of what the Messengers brought and its followers. And the purpose of the acts of worship which the Messengers commanded is to perfect the soul with love of God Almighty and devotedness to Him. Indeed, the soul has two powers - cognitive and practical. And these people made its perfection only in knowledge, then they thought that is knowledge of absolute existence until man becomes an intellect in potentiality parallel to the existing world. And among them are those who say: The soul only remains by the subsistence of its known object, and they believe in the subsistence of the spheres, intellects, and souls. So they made its perfection in knowledge of the existents whose subsistence they believed. And whoever approaches Islam among them says: Rather, its perfection is in knowledge of the Necessary Existent, and this resembles the saying of Jahm bin Safwan and those who agreed with him that 'faith is mere knowledge of God.' And we have expanded the speech on this in other places in the answer to 'the Safadian question' and elsewhere, and we explained that they erred in respects, including their assumption that the perfection of the soul is in mere knowledge; and their assumption that this perfection is obtained by knowledge of universal matters, not specific existents; and their assumption that what they have in theology is knowledge, while most of it is ignorance. Hence, the goal for them was assimilation to the sphere. Hence, whoever among them classifies concerning prayer, the purpose of it is not worship of God, nor is the purpose of prayer supplication to Him, since He does not know particulars according to them, nor does He distinguish between the one praying and the one not praying. Rather, the purpose of prayer is knowledge of absolute existence, which they claim is the perfection of the soul. And the outward prayer is sought for the governance and discipline of the body. And they said that the reality of prayer is knowledge of God Almighty of His oneness, necessity of existence, transcendence of His essence, and sanctification of His attributes in the flashes of sincerity in his prayer - p. 8. So know that prayer is divided into two parts - a part that is outward = The purpose is The Book of Refutation of the Logicians: He asks the moon and seeks refuge from it, for it manages this world through the active intellect. So it is according to them the lord who is asked and sought refuge from, and from it sciences overflow to the prophets and others. And perhaps they said: The purpose of prayer is to remember the Sharia which the Lawgiver legislated to preserve the law, remembering the Sharia which He legislated for them for the benefit of the world, as Ibn Sina and others mention. That is because they do not affirm according to them the truth that God hears the speech of servants, nor sees their actions, nor answers their supplication. Rather, supplication according to them is the soul's manipulation in the matter of the world, so it obtains by what it cares about from its detachment from the body a type of detachment until it manipulates the matter of the world. As for the Lord Almighty, He is not according to them knowing of all things, nor powerful over all things, nor does He know secret or whispered discourse or other than that of the states of servants, nor does He have many angels descending and ascending to Him according to them, nor does good speech or righteous deed ascend to Him, and the utmost of souls according to them is to be connected to the active intellect, which is their lord, not to ascend to God. The intended meaning of vision: And when they say the happiness of the soul is to witness God and see Him, the reality of that according to them is knowledge of what they conceived of absolute existence or of the existence of the Necessary Existent. And the author of 'the books withheld from those not worthy of them' when he speaks about the vision of the Truth and the vision of His face in his book 'al-Ihya' or elsewhere.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the philosophers' (falasifa) understanding of the purpose of prayer and the perfection of the soul. He begins by setting the context: the philosophers' claim that the world is pre-eternal (qadim) like their master Aristotle and his followers. He then asks how the wisdom (hikma) that God commanded His Prophet to call to could be this. He states that their wisdom aims to adjust the soul's morals to prepare it for knowledge, which they consider its perfection. However, this does not even complete the least of what the prophets brought. The true purpose of worship commanded by the prophets is to perfect the soul through love of God and devotion to Him (tahalluh). Ibn Taymiyya notes that the soul has two powers: cognitive (ilmiyya) and practical (amaliyya). The philosophers restrict perfection to the cognitive alone, and they imagine that this knowledge is knowledge of absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq), such that a person becomes a pure intellect parallel to the existing world. Some of them say the soul subsists by the subsistence of its known objects, and they believe in the subsistence of the celestial spheres, intellects, and souls, so they place perfection in knowledge of those enduring existents. Among those who try to align with Islam (al-mutaqarribun ila al-Islam), some say perfection is in knowledge of the Necessary Existent (Wajib al-Wujud), resembling the Jahmiyya who define faith as mere knowledge of God. Ibn Taymiyya states he has elaborated elsewhere (in his answer to the Safadian question) on their errors: (1) assuming perfection is merely in knowledge, (2) assuming it is attained through universal concepts rather than specific existents, and (3) assuming their theology is knowledge when most is ignorance. Consequently, their ultimate goal becomes assimilation to the celestial sphere (tashabbuh bi-l-falak). Hence, when they write about prayer, they do not intend worship of God or supplication to Him, because according to them God does not know particulars and does not distinguish between the one praying and the one not praying. Rather, their intended purpose of prayer is knowledge of absolute existence, which they claim is the soul's perfection. The outward prayer is merely for the discipline and training of the body. They claim the reality of prayer is knowledge of God's oneness, necessity, transcendence, etc., as quoted from Ibn Sina. Ibn Taymiyya then critiques their view of supplication: according to them, God does not hear servants nor see their actions nor answer prayers. Instead, supplication is the soul's manipulation of the world's matter (hayula) through detachment from the body. The Lord (al-Rabb) for them is not all-knowing or all-powerful; rather, the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al) is the one that manages the world and is asked from. They do not affirm angels descending and ascending, nor that good speech or righteous deeds ascend to God. The ultimate goal for souls is to connect with the active intellect, not to ascend to God. When they speak of the vision of God (ru'yat Allah), they interpret it as knowledge of absolute existence or of the Necessary Existent. Ibn Taymiyya then references the author of 'the books withheld from those not worthy of them' (likely al-Ghazali) discussing the vision of the Truth in al-Ihya or elsewhere, implying that even al-Ghazali's esoteric interpretations align with the philosophers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what role does the active intellect ('aql fa''al) play in the philosophers' view?
A) It is a metaphor for the soul's cognitive capacity
B) It is the lord that is asked and sought refuge from, managing the world and dispensing sciences
C) It is a lower angel that merely records deeds
D) It is the equivalent of the human intellect after death

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' system effectively substitutes the active intellect for God, denying God's knowledge of particulars and reducing supplication to a material manipulation, thus deviating from the core of Islamic worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
A philosopher says: 'When we pray, we are connecting to the active intellect, which is the source of all knowledge.' Write a response using Ibn Taymiyya's argument that this replaces God with a created entity and strips God of His attributes.
?
Read a passage from Ibn Sina's 'al-Isharat' where he discusses prayer. Identify elements that Ibn Taymiyya would criticize as substituting the active intellect for God.
